People v. Ruppert


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Westchester County


53 Misc. 2d 845; 279 N.Y.S.2d 895; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1572



April 26, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought to dismiss a 25-count indictment and to compel the production of certain records pertaining to the grand jury panel and a hearing to support the contentions in the motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that N.Y. Judiciary Law § 596, § 609(1), and § 661 were unconstitutional and that discriminatory practices in administering the rules, regulations and statutes of the Judiciary Law by the county commissioner of jurors were detrimental and prejudicial to his rights. The court denied the motion to dismiss the indictment and for production of the documents, holding that the challenged sections of the Judiciary Law were not pertinent to the issue sought to be raised. The first two related solely to New York City and the last was a form for a proposed questionnaire. The unsupported charges of dereliction on the part of the public official were insufficient to overcome the presumption that those charged with the administration of justice performed their duties properly. There was not one iota of fact to be found in the affidavit, even as to the sources of the information and belief. Defendant's challenge of the juror qualifications standard of the New York law was rejected as there needed to be some reasonable standards of qualifications and there must be a reasonable uniformity of application.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motions to dismiss the indictment, to compel the production of records, and for a hearing were denied.


HEADNOTES

Grand jury -- qualifications of jurors -- requirement that grand jurors own $ 250 worth of personalty or realty is constitutional; defendant's motion for hearing and for production of records denied.

Motion of defendant for the production of the Grand Jury list and records pertaining to the panel, and for a hearing on his attorney's conclusory allegations that the county Commissioner of Jurors discriminates against minority groups and the poor in administering the provisions of the Judiciary Law and the rules governing the selection of grand jurors, is denied. The statutory requirement that jurors own $ 250 worth of personalty or realty is reasonable and constitutional.

 

2088 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carmichael


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of New York, Town of Oakfield, Genesee County


53 Misc. 2d 584; 279 N.Y.S.2d 272; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1569



April 26, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The charge is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appeared in the trial court (New York) to answer the charge against him of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 381(6) for operating a motorcycle without a protective helmet, and alleged that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 381(6) for operating his motorcycle without a helmet. Defendant appeared in court to respond to the charge and alleged that the statute was unconstitutional. The court agreed, dismissing the charge against defendant. The court held that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 381(6), which required the operator of a motorcycle to wear a protective helmet, was unconstitutional as applied to defendant because it was not sufficiently definite to sustain a criminal conviction, and because the state's police power did not authorize statutes requiring a citizen to protect his own physical well-being. The court found that the police power traditionally did not include the power to make a citizen protect his own physical well-being and that to have held otherwise would have enlarged the police power beyond traditional limits. The court found that there has been no regulation for the sole purpose of making a state's citizens protect their own physical well-being so that others may have benefitted from it.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of defendant, dismissed the charge against him, and found that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to defendant.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- motorcycles -- Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 381, subd. 6), requiring motorcyclists to wear reflectorized protective helmets, is unconstitutional and void; charge dismissed.

The Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 381, subds. 6, 9, eff. Jan. 1, 1967) makes it "unlawful * * * for any person to operate or ride upon a motorcycle unless he wears a protective helmet of a type approved by the commissioner. Such a helmet must be equipped with either a neck or chin strap and be reflectorized on both sides thereof. The commissioner is hereby authorized and empowered to adopt and amend regulations covering the types of helmets and the specifications therefor and to establish and maintain a list of approved helmets which meet the specifications as established hereunder" (subd. 6); and makes it unlawful "to sell, offer for sale or distribute any protective helmets, goggles or face shields for use by the operators of motorcycles, or protective helmets for the use of passengers thereon, unless they are of a type and specification approved by the commissioner and appear on the list of approved devices maintained by the commissioner" (subd. 9). The [***2] Commissioner of Motor Vehicles has promulgated regulations ( 15 NYCRR Part 54) which apparently are directed only to the manufacturers and sellers and not to the wearers of helmets. While subdivision 9 of section 381 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which is directed to manufacturers and sellers, is undoubtedly valid, subdivision 6 which applies to persons who "operate or ride upon a motorcycle" is unconstitutional and void, for two reasons: (a) a person cannot be required to make an unreasonable effort to find out just what he is forbidden to do under criminal penalties; and (b) a person cannot be required, under the police power and criminal penalties, to protect himself by means which do not affect the safety of other persons. Therefore, the charge against defendant motorcyclist of violating subdivision 6 of section 381 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law is dismissed.

 

2089 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Simon v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, New York County


53 Misc. 2d 622; 279 N.Y.S.2d 223; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1603



April 17, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorcyclist brought an action against defendant City of New York to recover $ 167 in damages he claims to have sustained as a result of the negligence of the city in attempting to tow his illegally parked motorcycle.


OVERVIEW: The motorcyclist's vehicle was damaged by improper handling when a city crew attempted to remove it from a no parking zone. The motorcyclist filed a claim with the city comptroller's office and brought an action for damages. The court found in favor of the motorcyclist. It held that his damages were caused solely by the negligence of the city, and that he was not guilty of contributory negligence by virtue of violating a traffic regulation since that violation was not the proximate cause of the damages. The court awarded $ 117 in damages to the motorcycle but denied the motorcyclist's claim for lost income. While the city was authorized to tow away illegally parked motor vehicles, it had to do so in a reasonably prudent manner under the circumstances. The authority to tow did not give the city the license to destroy by neglect or otherwise. The city had never instructed the particular tow truck crew as to the proper way to tow a motorcycle. To justify their actions, there would have had to have been a showing of a specific emergency beyond a generally difficult traffic situation. At the time, the motorcycle did not create any obstruction than a utility bin next to it.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the motorcyclist as to the damages to his motorcycle but denied his claim for lost income.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- damage to towed-away motor vehicle -- city is liable for damage negligently caused to motor vehicle in towing it away from tow-away zone.

In a tow-away zone in New York City, plaintiff's new motorcycle was illegally parked between the sidewalk and a parked Consolidated Edison Company storage bin. It did not immediately obstruct any ambulance or fire engine or other emergency vehicle. The city properly removed the motorcycle at once, but improperly and negligently damaged it in lifting it into the tow truck by means of a hook and chain slung around the gas tank of the motorcycle. The proper binding is a cable or strap or net and precautions should be taken to prevent the motorcycle from swinging against the body of the truck. Plaintiff is awarded $ 117.73 damages to his motorcycle.

United States Flag Foundation, Inc. v. Radich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


53 Misc. 2d 597; 279 N.Y.S.2d 233; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1618



April 11, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a nonprofit tax-exempt organization formed to promote the display of and respect for the United States flag, sued defendant, an operator of an art gallery, to recover damages under N.Y. Penal Law § 1425(16). The gallery operator moved to dismiss the action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211(a)(3), (7).


OVERVIEW: The nonprofit contended that the gallery operator had exhibited two objects made partly of the United States flag that violated N.Y. Penal Law § 1425(16). The operator claimed that the nonprofit did not have the legal capacity to sue and that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. The court found that the facts alleged constituted a cause of action pursuant to the provisions of § 1425(16) and that the operator had completely failed to establish that the section was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied the operator's motion to dismiss the action.


HEADNOTES

Flags -- desecration -- action for damages for improper display of flag is sufficient (Penal Law, § 1425, subd. 16) -- section not unconstitutional; desecration of flag as symbolic act for expressing disagreement with Government improper.

1. A nonprofit, tax-exempt organization formed to promote the display of and respect for the United States flag has sufficiently alleged a cause of action to recover damages under subdivision 16 of section 1425 of the Penal Law against the operator of an art gallery who has exhibited "constructions" using the United States flag.

2. The section is not unconstitutional as denying freedom of speech, as vague, as violating the equal protection clause or as placing defendant in double jeopardy. The statute deals with the flag itself and in no way curtails political dissent or prohibits communication of ideas. The desecration of the flag cannot be utilized as a symbolic act to publish or exhibit disagreement with or opposition to the policies of the Government.

Irwin v. Board of Regents


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


53 Misc. 2d 430; 279 N.Y.S.2d 69; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1636



April 4, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Board of Regents of the University of the State of New York, sought to dismiss the N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding brought by petitioner accountant to reverse and rescind an order of the Commissioner of Education, which revoked the accountant's certificate to practice accountancy as a certified public accountant.


OVERVIEW: Charges were brought against the accountant alleging that he had been convicted of a crime within the purview and meaning of N.Y. Educ. Law § 7406(1)(c), and he was therefore guilty of unprofessional conduct. His requests at the hearing for subpoenas were denied. The court granted the accountant's petition, ordered the Commissioner of Education to rescind and cancel the order issued on behalf of the Board, respondent, and ordered that a new hearing be held at which the accountant was to be afforded a realistic opportunity to develop his defenses to the charges laid against him by the introduction of evidence. The refusal to issue subpoenas was arbitrary as the accountant might well have been able to establish through evidence upon the hearing much of his defense. In addition, other facts might have been developed which would have compelled a determination that the proceeding brought against him constituted an unjustifiable discrimination in contravention of the equal protection clauses of the Federal and State Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The Commissioner of Education was ordered to rescind and cancel the order revoking the accountant's certificate and to hold a new hearing at which the accountant was to be afforded a realistic opportunity to develop his defenses.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Licenses -- certified public accountants -- revocation annulled and new hearing directed; record should show whether or not discipline imposed is abuse of discretion; accountant's right to have subpoenas issued should not be denied by committee arbitrarily.

Revocation of a certified public accountant's certificate is annulled and a new hearing is directed, in which the record should show whether or not the measure of discipline imposed constitutes an abuse of discretion ( CPLR 7803, subd. 3), and at which hearing the accountant's rights "to have subpoenas issued by the committee" (Education Law, § 7406, subd. 3) should not be denied arbitrarily merely because the accountant wishes to prove that the gratuity which he gave was not such as to constitute "unprofessional conduct" or such as to violate "the consensus of opinion of the accountancy profession" and that the crime of which he was convicted was not "of fraud, deceit or gross negligence" (cf. Education Law, § 7406, subd. 1) and that the rules or regulations under which his certificate was revoked were not officially published as required by the State Constitution (art. IV, § 8) and the Executive Law ( § 102).

 

2092 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Combs v. La Vallee


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Cayuga County


53 Misc. 2d 281; 278 N.Y.S.2d 287; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1657



March 28, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons stated, the application is denied and the writ of habeas corpus applied for is disallowed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, an inmate in a state prison, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that the hearing procedure used by the parole board at his parole revocation hearing violated the Due Process and Right to Counsel Clauses of the New York and United States Constitutions. Respondent was the warden of the prison.


OVERVIEW: Relator was released on parole after serving part of a sentence for second degree manslaughter. He was declared delinquent as of a day later for failure to report to his parole officer. Following extradition proceedings in New Jersey, he was returned to prison. The parole board held a hearing with respect to the alleged violation of parole, determined that relator was a parole violator, and remanded him to serve the balance of his sentence. Relator claimed that the board's refusal to permit him to have counsel at the hearing violated his constitutional rights. The court denied the writ, holding that under N.Y. Correct. Law § 218, he was not entitled to counsel at the parole hearing. The procedure did not contravene relator's constitutional right to counsel. Relator was guaranteed counsel in all criminal prosecutions. His guilt or innocence had been determined at trial. The parole revocation hearing was held only to determine whether or not relator had violated the terms of his parole and whether he should be returned to prison. Because relator left the State without permission and did not report to his parole officer it affirmatively appeared that he violated his parole.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


HEADNOTES

Parole -- violation of parole -- omission of mandate by which relator is held is defect in habeas corpus petition but defect is waived where such information is available -- relator's constitutional rights not violated by refusing him counsel at parole violation hearing -- Parole Board's action is discretionary and not reviewable in court if performed according to law.

1. A petition for a writ of habeas corpus is defective for failure to annex thereto a copy of the mandate by which relator is detained as required by CPLR 7002 (subd. [c], par. 1). The defect is waived where the necessary facts are gleaned from the petition and reported court opinions involving relator.

2. Defendant was released on parole and then violated the conditions of his parole. At the hearing called by the Parole Board pursuant to section 218 of the Correction Law, the Parole Board followed the mandate of the statute in not permitting relator to be represented by counsel and he was not deprived of any right under the Federal and State Constitutions thereby. A parole violation hearing is [***2] not a criminal prosecution and no right to counsel exists in favor of the parole violator.

3. Whether the parole violator should be required to serve the balance of his term in State prison or outside the prison under supervised control is a discretionary matter for the Parole Board and its action is not reviewable by the courts if done in accordance with law (Correction Law, § 212).

Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County

This information was conveyed to the complainant, who then filed a complaint with the commission. After the commission found the landlords violated N.Y. City Admin. On review, the court denied the landlord's application to vacate and set aside the commission's order, and granted the commission's cross-motion for enforcement, because review of the entire record revealed sufficient evidence to support the factual findings and conclusions of the commission.

Civil rights -- discrimination in housing -- order granted in enforcement of order of New York City Commission on Human Rights directing landlords to rent certain apartment to Negro -- New York City law on human rights (Administrative Code of City of New York, § B1-7.0 et seq.) constitutional.

1. 2. The New York City law on human rights (Administrative Code of City of New York, § B1-7.0 et seq.) is valid and constitutional ( General Municipal Law, § 239-s).

 

2094 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. La Belle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Rensselaer County


53 Misc. 2d 111; 277 N.Y.S.2d 847; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1725



March 3, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for an order granting him a hearing to determine whether his custodial statement was taken in violation of Miranda.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. His conviction was reversed and remanded for retrial. Prior to his second trial, defendant filed a motion for an order granting him a hearing to determine whether a statement he made while in custody was taken in violation of the recent Miranda decision. The court denied the motion on the ground the Miranda decision did not apply retroactively. Miranda applied only to cases in which the trial began after the date it was decided. While defendant's second trial did not begin until after the Miranda decision was made, he was a criminal defendant well before the date of the decision.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- pretrial statement -- whether statement taken from defendant prior to decision in Miranda v. Arizona (384 U.S. 436) complied with constitutional requirements therein enunciated must be determined by court at pretrial hearing -- requirements of Miranda v. Arizona (supra) not applicable on retrial of defendant -- defendant's motion for hearing as to whether statement was taken in compliance with Miranda v. Arizona is denied.

1. Whether a statement taken from defendant in 1963, prior to the decision in Miranda v. Arizona (384 U.S. 436) was taken in compliance with defendant's constitutional rights as there indicated must be determined by the court in a pretrial hearing.

2. The procedural requirements of Miranda v. Arizona (supra) are applicable to trials occurring after the rendition of the decision but is not applicable, as here, to a retrial of defendant ordered on an appeal.

3. Defendant's motion for a hearing to determine whether the statement taken from him violated his constitutional rights as outlined in Miranda v. Arizona (supra) is denied especially since he had a pretrial hearing on the voluntariness of his statement.

 

2095 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Henrietta v. Fairchild


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


53 Misc. 2d 862; 279 N.Y.S.2d 992; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1765



February 17, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Town of Henrietta sought a declaratory judgment that defendant property owner violated the town's Zoning Ordinance by operating a boarding or rooming house in an area zoned for single-family residential use and an injunction against using the property for any purpose except those set forth in the applicable sections of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owner, a bachelor, lived in a house in a district zoned for single-family residential use with three to seven other young men, all but one of whom were bachelors. The other residents of the house paid a share for the upkeep of the property. The town sought a declaratory judgment that the use violated Henrietta, N.Y. Zoning Ordinance, and an injunction against such use of the property. The property owner contended that his use conformed to the ordinance, and that the ordinance was unconstitutional as to him. The court granted the relief requested by the town. The court held that the language of permissive occupation of such property as a "single family dwelling" under the ordinance could not have properly been construed as intended to sanction the use being made by defendant under the collective economic arrangement. The court concluded that the property owner's status was similar to a boarding house keeper, notwithstanding the ingenious form of his economic arrangement. Considering the ordinary and commonly accepted meaning of the term "single family dwelling" in light of the objectives of the ordinance such an approach was unrealistic and without merit.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the property owner's premises were being used in violation of the town ordinance, granted the town's request for an injunction against keeping, maintaining, and operating and using the premises for a boarding house or rooming house, or any purposes except those set forth in the ordinance. The court noted that the relief did not bar the property owner from seeking a zoning variance.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- occupancy of one-family dwelling by about seven bachelors who share expenses makes it rooming house or boarding house; injunction granted.

Plaintiff town is granted judgment enjoining defendant, a bachelor, from using his house, which is situated in a one-family dwelling zone, as a boarding house or rooming house. He collects from each of three to seven young men who reside with him monthly amounts for payments towards the mortgage, taxes, insurance, maintenance, and interior furnishings, and for the cost, apparently without any profit, of food, beer and entertainment. Each member of this group pays to defendant $ 75 a month plus an equal part of any monthly deficiency. Defendant keeps three or four automobiles on the premises, and the other members of the group usually keep about three more automobiles on the premises. This is not a single family dwelling use; rather, it is a use as a boarding house or rooming house in violation of the zoning ordinance.

 

2096 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Terrell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Bronx County


53 Misc. 2d 32; 277 N.Y.S.2d 926; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1770



February 15, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] That portion of the motion which seeks an inspection of the Grand Jury minutes is denied with leave to the defendants to renew at the trial of the action herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to suppress tangible evidence and admissions allegedly obtained from them by police during the course of a raid made without a warrant upon a multiple-dwelling residence.


OVERVIEW: Police officers positioned themselves on the fire escape of a multiple-dwelling residence and observed through a window what they believed to be drug trafficking activities in defendants' apartment. After alerting other officers, the observing officers turned the doorknob to the apartment and the door opened from within, revealing no indication of any illegal activity, and the officers went to the bedroom to search it. Defendants filed a motion to suppress the contraband seized and admissions subsequently obtained, claiming that such resulted from an illegal trespass within the curtilage of the apartment, which made the search, seizure, and arrests of defendants unconstitutional. The court granted the motion, holding that the observations surreptitiously made by the officers from the fire escape, which created the probable cause to search, were made in the course of a trespass upon the curtilage of the apartment and were thus illegal, probable cause having been illegally acquired. The court found that the officers' entrance into the apartment without a warrant was illegal and violative of the Fourth Amendment and thus all evidence and admissions obtained thereby were suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to suppress all the contraband seized and admissions obtained by the police in an illegal search of defendants' apartment, but denied with leave to renew at trial the portion of the motion seeking an inspection of the grand jury minutes.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawful searches and seizures and admissions -- fire escape adjoining apartment window is appurtenance or curtilage of residentially leased premises; officers who, without any warrant or probable cause, peered into window from fire escape were illegally searching apartment by trespass; any packaging of heroin they thus saw could not furnish reasonable cause for their subsequent entry and search of apartment; contraband which they seized in such raid is ordered suppressed from evidence -- admissions obtained from defendants in apartment are ordered suppressed, since they were not warned of their constitutional rights while in custody prior to formal arrest -- insufficient warning was given to defendant who made written statement, hence it too is suppressed -- arrests occurred prior to June 13, 1966, but this hearing took place after that date -- at trial defendants may renew their motion to inspect Grand Jury minutes.

1. Without a search warrant, and apparently without any preceding probable cause, law-enforcement [***2] officers surreptitiously unlatched the roof door of a multiple dwelling and entered upon the roof and went down the fire escape and, from the fire escape, peered into the recessed window of the bona fide residential apartment of 2 of the 15 subsequently arrested defendants. This constituted an unauthorized search by trespass of whatever they could see. The Multiple Dwelling Law ( § 53) indicates that the portion of a fire escape adjoining an apartment window is a necessary appurtenance of the apartment; hence it constitutes part of the curtilage of the residentially leased premises. The officers saw several women apparently putting heroin into bags; but since this evidence was obtained by the officers by an illegal trespass, it could not lawfully furnish reasonable cause for the officers' subsequent actions. The officers went around to the front door of the apartment and drew their guns and turned the knob of the apartment door, and thereupon the door opened. They entered the apartment and saw nothing illegal in view. They then went into the rear bedroom and searched there. Thus, by means of illegal trespasses they found and seized contraband. Such searches and seizures and [***3] the subsequent arrests of the defendants violated the defendants' rights under the Fourth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The physical evidence seized in this raid is therefore ordered suppressed.

2. Oral admissions made in the apartment by the 2 tenants and by 5 of the other defendants, all of whom were already in custody prior to their formal arrest, were obtained as the result of the officers' illegal trespass and their illegal failure to warn the defendants that they had the right to remain silent and to have a lawyer present, etc., as set forth in Miranda v. Arizona (384 U.S. 436, decided June 13, 1966); and a written statement was taken from 1 defendant after he had been insufficiently warned. These arrests were made prior to June 13, 1966; but this hearing has been held since that date. All of the statements are ordered suppressed.

3. Defendants' motion to inspect the Grand Jury minutes is denied but it may be renewed at the trial.

 

2097 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Depaul v. Berkowitz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Utica, Oneida County


54 Misc. 2d 156; 281 N.Y.S.2d 449; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1775



February 14, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] However, the motion made by the District Attorney to withdraw the information is granted, and the defendant is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss an information that charged him with violating the Sabbath Law, N.Y. Penal Law § 2147. The district attorney filed a motion to withdraw the information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a drug store that sold medicines and various other items. Defendant was charged with violating the Sabbath Law, N.Y. Penal Law § 2147, when he sold two bottles of gas line antifreeze on a Sunday. The district attorney moved to withdraw the charge when he found that defendant and other merchants had begun to observe the Sabbath Law. Defendant refused to join in the motion, instead requesting that the district attorney specify which items could be sold on a Sunday. When the district attorney declined to do so, defendant filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that it was impossible to discern from § 2147 which items could be sold on a Sunday. In denying defendant's motion, the court pointed out that § 2147 permitted gasoline to be sold on a Sunday but held that gas line antifreeze, although made from petroleum, was not a gasoline product. The court stated that the exceptions to § 2147 were to be narrowly construed so as to give credence to New York's stated public policy of setting aside Sunday as a day of repose.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion and granted the district attorney's motion. As a result, defendant was discharged.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sales on Sunday -- "gasoline" which may be sold on Sunday as exception within Penal Law ( § 2147) does not include dry gas, petroleum distillate product; dismissal of information denied.

"Gasoline", which may be sold on Sunday under the Sabbath Law ( Penal Law, § 2147) as one of the exceptions therein, should not be expanded to include all petroleum distillates, including a dry gas (gas line anti-freeze) sold by defendant. Defendant's motion to dismiss the information charging him with violation of section 2147 on the ground that the item sold was excepted therefrom is denied and the District Attorney's motion to withdraw the information is granted.

 

2098 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smallwood


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Special Sessions of New York, Town of Irondequoit, Monroe County


52 Misc. 2d 1027; 277 N.Y.S.2d 429; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1785



February 14, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Subdivision 6 of section 381 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law is unconstitutional; complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a complaint filed against him for the charge of violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 381(6). Defendant was arrested for wearing a knitted-ski-type hat with no chin or neck strap and no reflectors while driving a motorcycle. Defendant argued that § 381(6) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Upon defendant's trial for not wearing a protective helmet, he challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The Legislature left the decision of what type of helmet would be approved to the will of the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles of the State of New York. Accordingly, the court found that § 381(6) was too indefinite. The court held that laws had to be so explicit that all men subject to their penalties knew what acts it was their duty to avoid. It was definite that such a "protective helmet" be equipped with a neck or chinstrap and further that it must be "reflectorized" on both sides. The motorist had no other warning of what he had to wear, except that the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles had to approve it. It became incumbent upon the operator or rider, to obtain somewhere, a list of approved helmets, and the list had to be kept current because the Commissioner could amend the list. Furthermore, the statute did not require this stated safety device for the purpose of protecting other users of the highways from injuries or damage; it simply removed from the individual the right to exercise his judgment, or preference, in the use of personal adornment.


OUTCOME: The court found the statute under which defendant was arrested unconstitutional and dismissed the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- motorcycles -- Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 381, subd. 6), requiring motorcyclists to wear reflectorized protective helmets, and empowering Commissioner of Motor Vehicles to adopt and amend regulations and lists of approved helmets, is unclear and unconstitutional; hence information dismissed.

A criminal statute which does not state clearly what is forbidden is unconstitutional and void. Such a statute is subdivision 6 of section 381 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which states as follows: "It shall be unlawful, on and after January first, nineteen hundred sixty-seven, for any person to operate or ride upon a motorcycle unless he wears a protective helmet of a type approved by the commissioner. Such a helmet must be equipped with either a neck or chin strap and be reflectorized on both sides thereof. The commissioner is hereby authorized and empowered to adopt and amend regulations covering the types of helmets and the specifications therefor and to establish and maintain a list of approved helmets which meet the specifications as established hereunder."  [***2] An information charging that defendant did not wear a protective and reflectorized helmet while operating a motorcycle is dismissed.

 

2099 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Greenburgh v. Board of Supervisors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


53 Misc. 2d 88; 277 N.Y.S.2d 885; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1804



February 3, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county board of supervisors filed a motion for approval of a local law adopting a reapportionment plan for the composition of the board in an action by plaintiffs, town, town board, and citizens' groups, challenging the plan on the ground that it denied to the county's citizens equal protection of the laws as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The county was composed of 18 towns and six cities, which had different population levels. Each town had one representative on the county's board of supervisors, with each member having one vote with equal voting power. The town filed an action alleging that this system caused an inequity in representation that violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and New York Constitutions.The court granted summary judgment in favor of the town, declaring the apportionment of voting power in the board was unconstitutional. The board adopted a reapportionment plan and filed a motion seeking approval of the local law incorporating the plan. The court denied the motion and declared the law to be unconstitutional. The court held that the law's combination of weighted voting and multimember electoral districts failed to provide substantially equal population-based representation to the voters under the "one person, one vote" principle, which resulted in invidious discrimination that was prohibited by the Equal Protection Clauses. In other respects, the court held that unconstitutionality of the reapportionment law had not been sufficiently demonstrated.


OUTCOME: The court denied the board's motion for approval of the law adopting the reapportionment plan for the composition of the board.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Board of Supervisors -- representation of people must be based on total number of residents in district, not merely on number of registered voters in district -- unequally populated districts of county may be represented on county board by unequal numbers of legislators and by unequal weights given to votes of such legislators at meetings of county board, so that each vote cast at meetings of county board will represent substantially same number of people -- residents of incorporated villages may be represented by their town legislators -- no unconstitutional discrimination results from applying requirement of Town Law ( § 23), which is not in city Charters, that legislators must be real property owners -- local law of county, reapportioning Supervisors of 18 towns and 6 cities, is adjudged unconstitutional, on sole ground that ward lines in 2 cities are based only on registration of voters.

1. The total number of residents in a district -- not merely the number of residents who were registered as voters in any preceding election -- is the number which must be counted in order to determine that each resident of that district has no more [***2] or less than one vote as compared with any resident of any other district. Therefore, a local law reapportioning the Supervisors who comprise a county Board of Supervisors is adjudged unconstitutional, on the ground that the ward lines for the election of supervisors in two of the cities are based on the number of registered voters only and that it appears that this error could result in variances of as much as 95%.

2. In all other respects, the right of the people to the equal protection of the laws (U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 11), which right is summarized in the phrase "one person, one vote", is not basically violated by the method which this local law proposes to use to apportion the population of the county. This method keeps, as district lines, the lines of the 18 towns and the lines of 4 of the cities and the ward lines of the other 2 cities, all of which have different populations, but provides that different numbers of legislators shall be elected at large from each of said districts, and further provides that the voting power exercised at meetings of the board by the legislators from the different districts shall be weighted so as to give the total [***3] of 54 legislators a total of 861 votes on the board, and so that each of said 861 votes at meetings of the board shall represent approximately 991 residents of the county.

3. This local law has been enacted by the current Board of Supervisors under the powers granted to them by the Constitution and the Municipal Home Rule Law and in conformity with the Town Law and the Westchester County Charter and the Westchester County Administrative Code. No unconstitutional discrimination, of sufficient substance to require annulment by the judicial branch of government, results (a) from the local law's failure to allow the residents of the incorporated villages to elect representatives other than their town representatives, or (b) from the local law's requirement that the town legislators be real property owners as provided in the Town Law ( § 23) for Supervisors, even though the Supervisors or legislators from the cities need not be real property owners since none of the city Charters requires it.

 

2100 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Panzer v. Berman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


53 Misc. 2d 122; 277 N.Y.S.2d 186; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1836



January 24, 1967 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application is denied, and the proceeding is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landlord brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, seeking review of a determination by respondent, city rent and rehabilitation administrator, that the landlord's housing accommodations did not qualify for rent decontrol. The administrator found that the conversion from a rooming house to "self-contained family units" was not timely and that the units failed to meet the regulatory requirements to qualify for decontrol.


OVERVIEW: The landlord owned rental property that he originally used as a rooming house. The rent control regulations in existence at the time provided that, if a rooming house was a slum, it was subject to rent control. Although the landlord contested that determination, another trial court previously found for the administrator. The landlord subsequently converted the property to "self-contained family units" and contended that the property was no longer in such a condition to be a slum and requested that it be decontrolled. The administrator found that the regulations had changed and that all rooming houses were subject to rent control and that the conversion did not meet the regulatory standards for conversion to qualify for decontrol. The court held that the housing accommodations created by conversion from rooming house accommodations could not qualify for decontrol under applicable regulations. The court concluded that there was sufficient ground in the record to support the administrator's determination that the housing accommodations were not converted before the regulatory deadline and that the "self-contained family units" did not meet the statutory requirements for decontrol.


OUTCOME: The court denied the landlord's application for rent decontrol and dismissed the proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- conversion of 12-room rooming house into 10 small apartments, completed after April 30, 1962, does not entitle landlord to decontrol (N. Y. City Rent, Eviction and Rehabilitation Regulations, § 11) -- Rent Administrator's denial of decontrol sustained -- orders of Special Term remanding matter to State Rent Administrator did not constitute judicial law of case, since law has been changed and all rooming house occupants have surrendered possession and landlord has leased newly created apartments to new tenants.

1. A landlord altered and converted a 12-room rooming house into a 10-family apartment house containing a total of approximately 20 rooms. The New York City Rent and Rehabilitation Administrator fixed the maximum rents of the apartments at the rentals agreed upon in the leases, and refused to decontrol the house. Such refusal of decontrol was proper, because (a) the conversion was not completed until "after April 30, 1962", (b) the conversion has not "resulted in additional housing accommodations consisting of self-contained family units", and (c) only 1 or 2 [***2] of the 10 apartments contains the required "minimum total area of 395 square feet exclusive of the area of bathrooms and closets." (N. Y. City Rent, Eviction and Rehabilitation Regulations, § 11, subd. a, pars. [1], [2]; § 11, subd. d; promulgated pursuant to Administrative Code of City of New York, § Y51-3.0, subd. e, par. 2, subpar. [i], cl. [2], and pursuant to Local Emergency Housing Rent Control Act [L. 1962, ch. 21], § 11.)

2. The City Rent and Rehabilitation Administrator's determination was properly based on the evidence and was not arbitrary or capricious, and hence the determination is sustained and this judicial review proceeding is dismissed (Administrative Code of City of New York, § Y51-9.0, subd. b; Local Emergency Housing Rent Control Act [L. 1962, ch. 21], § 8).

3. Earlier orders of Special Term of the Supreme Court, remanding the landlord's application to the State Rent Administrator, do not constitute the judicial law of the case, because, during the succeeding years during which this matter remained undetermined and inactive, the Legislature transferred rent control from the State Rent Administrator to the City of New York and the city established [***3] the office of City Rent and Rehabilitation Administrator and the latter promulgated the New York City Rent, Eviction and Rehabilitation Regulations, and because, furthermore, the rooming house occupants all surrendered possession and the landlord leased the newly created apartments to new tenants.

 

2101 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rubin v. McAlevey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Rockland County


54 Misc. 2d 338; 282 N.Y.S.2d 564; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1844



January 20, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners brought a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 for a declaration that defendant town's interim development law, Ramapo, N.Y., Local Law Nos. 2, 4, 6 (1966), was unconstitutional or in the alternative for a judgment annulling the decision of the town board denying a permit to erect a commercial building on the property owners' property as illegal, arbitrary, and capricious.


OVERVIEW: During the time that the property owners' land was conditionally rezoned in the highway business district, the town enacted an interim development law prohibiting the issuance of any building permits within the areas where zoning changes were contemplated until the effective date of the 1966 comprehensive amendment to the zoning law. The town board thereafter denied a variance for the construction of an automobile sales and service agency on the property owners' land. The court held that the interim zoning law was valid because (1) a locality could enact reasonable interim legislation prohibiting the commencement of construction for a reasonable time during consideration of proposed zoning changes; (2) the happening of the event that would terminate the stop-gap ordinance was determinable given that the 1966 comprehensive amendment had to be passed before December 31, 1966, and that the effective date of the amendment was 10 days after publication and posting of the same; and (3) the town board could issue special permits during the freeze period. The court further held that the denial of the application for the special permit was neither arbitrary nor capricious.


OUTCOME: The court held that the town's interim development law was constitutional and that the town board's denial of a special permit for construction of a commercial building on the property owners' land was not illegal, arbitrary, or capricious.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- interim law -- pursuant to local law prohibiting issuance of building permits until effective date of pending comprehensive zoning amendment and providing that variance might be granted meantime if approved by planning board, application for variance was properly denied.

The owners of a parcel of land which was zoned for residence and offices and special industries executed and recorded an agreement with the town in 1960 whereby the land was rezoned for highway business uses but upon certain conditions and restrictions, including the condition that the zoning would revert to its former classification, after publication and posting ( Town Law, § 265), if construction were not begun within two years. The agreement further provided that it could be modified by consent of both parties, and that it would expire in 20 years or upon the town's adoption of a comprehensive change in zoning, whichever occurred first. The owners were subsequently granted extensions until November 25, 1966 of the original two-year limit within which to commence construction. In May, 1966, they contracted to sell a portion of the land to an automobile sales and service [***2] agency. Meantime the town was preparing, with the aid of State and Federal agencies, a master plan for a comprehensive change in its entire zoning ordinance; and on June 2, 1966 and subsequently, the town enacted local laws prohibiting the issuance of any building permits within the areas, constituting some three fourths of the town, wherein changes were to be made by the master plan. Said plan was adopted as a comprehensive zoning ordinance on July 26, 1966, effective on December 31, 1966. Said local law further provided that, in the interim, any application to vary or modify the law's application as to any property would be referred to the town's Planning Board for a report as to the effect on the master plan, and that thereupon the Town Board would make a determination in its absolute legislative discretion. Pursuant to these provisions, and since the master plan would rezone this parcel as residential, the Town Board lawfully, constitutionally and properly denied the owners' application for a variance for an automobile sales and service building.

 

2102 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Croen v. Vetrano


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


52 Misc. 2d 915; 277 N.Y.S.2d 354; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1852



January 17, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town residents who did not own realty filed an action against defendant town supervisor, seeking a declaratory judgment that a law which prohibited them from voting in an election to determine whether the town incorporated as a village was unconstitutional, as well as injunctive relief barring the supervisor from enforcing the law. The residents filed a motion for summary judgment; the supervisor filed a motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The complaint attacked N.Y. Village Law § 3-316, which provided that in elections to determine whether an area chose to incorporate as a village, only residents who owned realty were qualified to vote. The town residents who did not own realty argued that § 3-316, and N.Y. Village Law art. 3 were discriminatory, and as such, violated the equal protection clauses of both the N.Y. Const. and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. In ordering the complaint dismissed, the court held that N.Y. Village Law art. 3 was constitutional. In so ruling, the court stressed the presumption of constitutionality accorded statutes, and found that the residents failed to make any factual showing that there was no reasonable basis for the qualification that only realty owners could vote in incorporation elections. The court also rejected the claim that the real property ownership qualification hinged upon one's wealth. Because it found nothing irrational, unreasonable, arbitrary or capricious in providing the qualification, there was no basis to rule that the qualification was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court denied the residents' motion for summary judgment, and dismissed the complaint. It also held that the statute in question was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- incorporation of village -- constitutional law -- Village Law ( § 3-316), limiting voters, on question of incorporating village, to those residents who own realty therein, is constitutional.

A part of a town may be incorporated as a village, upon the votes of those residents of such territory who are owners of real property in such territory (Village Law, art. 3, § 3-316). Such statutory limitation of voters is not discriminatory, irrational or unconstitutional. This action by residents who do not own realty in the territory, for a judgment declaring the statute unconstitutional, is dismissed.

 

2103 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Waldstreicher v. Michaelian


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


52 Misc. 2d 711; 276 N.Y.S.2d 758; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1873



January 10, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, county social workers, brought an article 78 proceeding on behalf of themselves and all other persons similarly situated, seeking to compel respondent county to grant them a salary increase pursuant to § 79-a of the Social Welfare Law, 1965 N.Y. Law 400.


OVERVIEW: The county contended that § 79(a), which required the county to increase the salaries of social workers with graduate training, was invalid and unconstitutional. The court disagreed. The salary advantage provided for under § 79-a did not constitute a promotion within the meaning and intent of N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 52(9); but even if it did, there was nothing in the constitution which prohibited the legislature from amending the Civil Service Law to the extent necessary to permit favored treatment to trained personnel. The term "other social service personnel" was not vague. Salaries paid to employees of local welfare departments were a matter of state concern, and consequently, the legislation in question was an exception to the home rule provisions. Section 79(a) of the Social Welfare Law on its face applied in like manner to all political subdivisions of the state and did not arbitrarily single out a particular community. The state department's failure to act and to implement the statute would not result in a denial to qualified persons of the statutory benefits. Employees who completed the necessary graduate training were entitled to the relief sought.


OUTCOME: The court granted the relief requested by the county social workers.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil service -- case workers -- compensation -- salary increase granted to case workers and social service workers who have graduate training by Social Welfare Law (§ 79-a) is not promotion -- section 79-a not vague in defining those entitled to increase or amount thereof -- statute does not violate home rule provisions of Constitution -- section is general law -- petitioners employed as case workers and supervisors are those intended to be benefited -- approval of "suitable graduate training" must be granted by local welfare department -- no difficulty in determining whether employee has required qualifications -- county does not have satisfactory alternative plan in lieu of higher salaries -- employees who have completed necessary graduate training are entitled to relief; issue as to whether any petitioner has completed training will be set down for trial.

1. Section 79-a was added to the Social Welfare Law and provides higher salaries (10% for one year of graduate training and 20% for two years) for case workers and other social service personnel employed by a local welfare department "who have suitable graduate training approved by the department". The salary increase [***2] provided by said section does not constitute a promotion within the meaning and intent of subdivision 9 of section 52 of the Civil Service Law. Even if it did, the Constitution does not prohibit the Legislature from amending the law to the extent necessary to permit favored treatment of trained personnel.

2. The statute is not vague in defining those entitled to the increase or the amount thereof.

3. The statute does not violate the home rule provisions of the Constitution. Salaries paid to employees of local welfare departments are a matter of State concern and therefore the legislation is an exception to such provisions.

4. The section is a general law applying to all political subdivisions of the State.

5. While the statute contemplates that the State Department of Social Welfare will adopt rules for carrying out some of the provisions of the statute, petitioners are employed as social case workers and supervisors and are those whom the Legislature intended to benefit.

6. The approval of "suitable graduate training" as required under the statute must be granted not by the State Department of Social Welfare but by the local welfare department, to which the word "department"  [***3] as used in the statute refers.

7. Whether an employee has "suitable graduate training" is not so vague as to require further definition. "Suitable" means training in the specialized field of social work. The local welfare department should have no difficulty in determining whether a person meets the required qualifications.

8. The county does not have a satisfactory alternative plan in lieu of the higher salaries. The statute expressly requires that the proposed alternative plan be submitted to the State Department of Social Welfare for approval. There is no evidence that any alternative plan has ever been approved.

9. Employees who have completed the necessary graduate training are entitled to the relief sought. If there is any issue between the parties as to whether any of the petitioners has completed such training, a hearing will be had to resolve the issue.

 

2104 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Freedman v. Suffolk County Board of Supervisors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


52 Misc. 2d 670; 276 N.Y.S.2d 746; 1967 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1889



January 4, 1967 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two proceedings under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, consolidated for purposes of disposition, petitioners, the employees of the Department of Public Welfare of Suffolk County and the Department of Social Welfare of Erie County, sought to require respondent employers to provide salary increases. The employers filed a motion to dismiss the petitions for failure to state facts sufficient to constitute grounds for the relief sought.


OVERVIEW: The employees argued that they were entitled to salary increased in accordance with N.Y. Soc. Welf. Law § 79-a. The employers countered that the statute was unconstitutional. The court first determined that the employers had standing to test the constitutionality of the statute in issue. It ruled that the statute was unconstitutional. The granting of a salary increase in the manner proposed by the statute constituted a promotion without first determining merit and fitness by competitive examination. The attempt to achieve that end violated the state constitution. The court ruled that although educational attainment could be used as a qualifying element for admission to a competitive examination, its use as a substitute for competition could not be condoned.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the employers.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil service -- case workers -- compensation -- in proceedings to compel counties to pay salary increases mandated by Social Welfare Law (§ 79-a) for case workers with graduate training, counties have standing to challenge constitutionality of statute -- section 79-a provides salary increase beyond limit of grade and constitutes promotion in violation of Constitution (art. V, § 6); section unconstitutional.

1. In proceedings by case workers in Social Welfare or Public Welfare Departments of counties to require the counties to provide salary increases mandated by section 79-a of the Social Welfare Law for those case workers and social service personnel having "suitable graduate training" to the extent of at least 10% for one year of such training and at least 20% for two years, the counties have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the section.

2. Section 6 of article V of the State Constitution requires that promotions be made according to merit and fitness to be ascertained by competitive examination. To grant increases by virtue of education constitutes a promotion without first determining merit and fitness by competitive examination in violation of the Constitution.  [***2] Moreover subdivision 9 of section 52 of the Civil Service Law provides that an increase of salary beyond the limit fixed for the grade shall be deemed a promotion, and section 79-a specifies no maximum limitation but only a minimum. Absent a ceiling on the increase, petitioners may exceed the confines of the grade and title. The section is unconstitutional.

 

2105 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Widziewicz v. Golding


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Dutchess County


52 Misc. 2d 837; 277 N.Y.S.2d 62; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1180



December 30, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a special proceeding (New York) under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 4 for relief under N.Y. County Law § 17-A, seeking certain records and information relating to a murder investigation. Respondents in the special proceeding were the district attorney and the county medical examiner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a defendant in a separate criminal case charging him with murder. Through the special civil proceeding petitioner sought to obtain certain information and records of the medical examiner. The court concluded that petitioner sought to gain disclosure of certain items of evidence in a civil proceeding which he was not entitled to as a defendant in the criminal proceeding. N.Y. County Law § 675(1) provided that the medical examiner had the authority, when necessary in his opinion, to request certain tests. The medical examiner was not required to perform certain tests. Petitioner was unable to obtain an analysis of sheeting allegedly used in the murder, since no such analysis was undertaken, and no such analysis was required. Additionally, under § 675 petitioner was unable to obtain the names of all persons consulted. Petitioner already had in his possession the names of the only witnesses who were present at the time of the investigation at the scene of the death. The medical examiner was not compelled to furnish to petitioner the transcripts of any testimony of witnesses examined by the medical examiner, and the request was denied.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- medical examiner's reports -- indicted defendant, who has been given copy of autopsy report and Medical Examiner's report of investigation made at scene where body was found, is not entitled to transcripts of testimony of any witnesses or to reports of any analyses of sheeting which was found tied around victim's neck -- lack of preliminary hearing before indictment does not entitle defendant to disclosure of evidence -- indicted defendant cannot obtain disclosure of evidence by means of civil proceeding (under CPLR, art. 4, and County Law, art. 17-A).

1. The County Law (art. 17-A, § 677, subd. 3, par. [b]) provides that the records of the Medical Examiner of the county are open to inspection by the District Attorney but that any other interested person must obtain a court order. This statute does not change the principle of criminal law that an indicted defendant is not entitled to disclosure of evidence or to statements of witnesses; and this principle of criminal law cannot be evaded by an indicted defendant's instituting a proceeding under the CPLR or under article 17-A of the County Law.

2. Defendant has been indicted for [***2] grand larceny and first degree murder. The District Attorney has given the defendant a complete copy of the Medical Examiner's autopsy report, which includes the findings of a pathologist, and which indicates that the victim was strangled with a piece of sheeting tied around her neck. Attached to this report is the Medical Examiner's report of his investigation made at the scene (County Law, § 674), which states that the deceased was found by her husband a considerable time after her death, that said husband called the police, and that there were no witnesses at the investigation at the scene except the police, an Assistant District Attorney, the Medical Examiner, and a physician. The Medical Examiner states that he has not examined any witnesses under oath and that he has not ordered any examinations or analyses of the sheeting or of any other objects (under County Law, §§ 674, 675). Such examinations are discretionary with the Medical Examiner; but even if made, they are not subject to inspection by an indicted defendant.

3. The fact that there was no preliminary Magistrate's hearing before the indictment does not entitle the defendant to inspect the Grand Jury minutes or to [***3] inspect the evidence against him.

4. Accordingly, defendant's petition against the Medical Examiner and the District Attorney, in the form of a civil proceeding (under CPLR, art. 4, and County Law, art. 17-A), for the names and addresses of all witnesses and for transcripts of their testimony and for reports of all analyses and examinations, is dismissed.

 

2106 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Angelica Co. v. Goodman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


52 Misc. 2d 844; 276 N.Y.S.2d 766; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1181



December 30, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The counterclaim is sufficient, and the motion to dismiss it is denied: the cross motion to dismiss the complaint is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mail order business filed a defamation action against defendant city. The city filed a counterclaim which sought an injunction, accounting, and damages resulting from misleading advertisements published by the mail order business. The mail order business filed a motion for dismissal of the counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: The city alleged that the mail order business refused to file information which resulted in the violation of the provisions of the Jenkins Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 375 et seq., thus encouraging violation of the city and state cigarette use tax provisions. In addition, it was argued that the corporation refused to make collection of cigarette use tax in violation of N.Y. Tax Law § 471 New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § D46-2.0, causing irreparable injury resulting from the misleading of purchasers into the false belief that their purchases were not subject to cigarette tax and rendering the collection of the tax extremely difficult if not impossible. The court found that these allegations made by the city stated a cause of action and refused to dismiss the counterclaim.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the counterclaim was denied.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- State and city cigarette taxes -- constitutional law -- libel -- fair comment -- any sale by mail from out of State to any New York State or New York City resident of any number of cigarettes, even less than 400, is taxable -- such tax laws are constitutional -- Federal act requiring mail-order sellers to co-operate with State tax authorities is constitutional -- provision in Federal act giving United States courts jurisdiction does not divest State courts of jurisdiction -- statement by New York City Finance Director that North Carolina corporation is bootlegging cigarettes into city is true, or at least is fair comment -- city may maintain counterclaim against North Carolina corporation for injunction, accounting and damages -- New York court has jurisdiction, constitutionally, to subject North Carolina plaintiff to counterclaim.

1. Any out-of-State mail sale of any number of cigarettes to a New York State or New York City resident is subject to the New York State and/or New York City cigarette tax; a sale of 400 cigarettes or less [***2] is exempt only when the cigarettes are personally brought into this State or city (Tax Law, §§ 471, 471-b; Administrative Code of City of New York, § D46-2.0).

2. The State and city cigarette tax laws are constitutional; they are not an unreasonable restraint upon interstate commerce.

3. The Jenkins Act (U.S. Code, tit. 15, § 375 et seq.), requiring mail-order sellers to file with the taxing States the names and addresses of purchasers and the quantities sold, is constitutional. The provision giving the United States District Courts jurisdiction to restrain violations of said act (U.S. Code, tit. 15, § 378) is not exclusive; the State courts too have jurisdiction.

4. When the New York City Finance Director issued a statement to the newspapers which, when read in full context, asserted that a certain North Carolina mail-order sales corporation was bootlegging cigarettes into New York City and New York State, he uttered truth, or at least fair comment. The corporation's allegation that he spoke maliciously is not enough; it has not shown any malice.

5. Accordingly, summary judgment is granted dismissing the North Carolina corporation's complaint against the City of New York [***3] and the city's Finance Director for damages for defamation; and the court denies the North Carolina corporation's motion to dismiss the counterclaim wherein an injunction and an accounting and damages are sought because of the corporation's violations of the State and city tax laws and the Jenkins Act.

6. The New York court has jurisdiction, constitutionally, to subject the North Carolina corporation to the counterclaim, since the corporation's advertisements here and business here constitute sufficient contacts with New York State.

 

2107 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Phelan v. Motor Vehicle Acci. Indemnification Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


52 Misc. 2d 341; 275 N.Y.S.2d 873; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1196



December 27, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to stay arbitration with respect to the claimant in her representative capacity is denied. It is conceded that the claimant in her individual capacity has no right to arbitration. The motion to permanently stay arbitration as to Joan Phelan, individually, is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent moved for leave to reargue the granting of an application by respondent to stay arbitration on a claim for wrongful death and pain and suffering where the automobile liability policy issued to the deceased contained a standard New York Automobile Accident Indemnification Endorsement.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's decedent, a New York City Department of Sanitation employee, while in the performance of his duties, was killed by an uninsured automobile. The decedent was an "insured" person under the standard New York Automobile Accident Indemnification Endorsement. At death, deceased was a member of the New York City Employees' Retirement System and, as such, the widow was awarded an annual accidental death pension. At issue was whether or not the court would judicially enlarge the language of the endorsement to equate payments made under a retirement or pension system with those made under a workmen's compensation law. The court held that the language of the endorsement referred only to "any workmen's compensation payments." The endorsement could not to be enlarged to include payments other than workmen's compensation payments. Thus, the motion to stay arbitration with respect to petitioner in her representative capacity was denied.


OUTCOME: The court denied respondent's motion to stay arbitration on the grounds that the language of the endorsement did not include payments other than workmen's compensation payments.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- Motor Vehicle Accident Indemnification Corporation -- MVAIC cannot reduce its liability by actuarial value of accidental death benefit payable to widow of member of New York City Employees' Retirement System.

Decedent was insured under an automobile liability policy which contained the standard New York automobile accident indemnification endorsement whereby the MVAIC agreed to pay him or his estate up to $ 10,000 for his injury or death wrongfully caused by an uninsured automobile. He was killed by an uninsured automobile while performing his duties as an employee of the City of New York. Pursuant to his contract with and his payments to the New York City Employees' Retirement System, his widow received the return of his accumulated payments or contributions plus an annual accidental death pension. The actuarial value of said pension far exceeds $ 10,000. Nevertheless, and even [***2] though the MVAIC endorsement provides that any amount payable by MVAIC shall be reduced by "the amount paid and the present value of all amounts payable on account of such bodily injury under any workmen's compensation law, exclusive of non-occupational disability benefits", MVAIC is not entitled to offset the value of this death benefit against its own $ 10,000 liability as the implied insurer of the uninsured tort-feasor.

 

2108 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Witherspoon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, Suffolk County


52 Misc. 2d 320; 275 N.Y.S.2d 592; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1236



December 13, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons hereinbefore set forth, the motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for an order dismissing the informations filed against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an outdoor advertising company, was charged with erecting certain signs without first having obtained the required permits. Defendant sought dismissal of the informations arguing that the permits were not necessary because the town's zoning powers did not extend to land owned by a state authority, the ordinance under attack is unconstitutional, and enforcement of the sign ordinance would be an unreasonable interference with interstate commerce. The court denied defendant's motion. The court held that the authority would be subject to the ordinance's regulation of signs in accordance with established standards in that the particular function at issue would be proprietary rather than governmental. The court further held that there was no constitutional infringement in enforcement of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the informations against it.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- billboards -- advertising company which leases land for its billboards from Metropolitan Commuter Transportation Authority may be prosecuted for violating town's ordinance which regulates billboards and which requires permit and fee.

A town's zoning ordinance which limits the size of any billboards and advertising signs and requires a permit from the town for the erection of such signs and the payment of a reasonable fee for such a permit, and imposes criminal penalties for failure to obtain a permit, validly applies to an advertising company which leases land from the Long Island Rail Road Company or from the railroad's statutory successor, the Metropolitan Commuter Transportation Authority (Public Authorities Law, §§ 1260-1278, as added by L. 1965, ch. 324). The ordinance does not unconstitutionally limit the State powers or governmental powers or land ownership of the Authority nor does it unreasonably burden national or interstate commerce. The fee for the permit is designed to defray the cost of administering the ordinance. The size of the sign allowed may be appealed to the [***2] town's Zoning Board of Appeals (Town Law, § 267). Accordingly, in this criminal prosecution of the advertising company for violating the zoning ordinance by failing to obtain permits, such defendant's motion for a dismissal of the information is denied.

 

2109 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gold v. Jacobi


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


52 Misc. 2d 491; 276 N.Y.S.2d 309; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1242



December 12, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The notice is accordingly modified by striking item 1.

The driver's license sought is properly discoverable under the circumstances of this case, and the motion to strike item 2 is therefore denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an automobile driver and its owner, filed a motion to vacate plaintiffs' notice of discovery seeking production of the driver's operator license and the owner's liability insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs served a notice of discovery on defendants that sought the production of the driver's license of defendant driver and the automobile liability insurance policy of defendant owner. Defendants filed a motion to vacate the notice. The court granted the motion to strike the production of defendant owner's automobile liability insurance policy. The court ruled that when the New York Civil Code was adopted, it took a more restrictive approach to pretrial disclosure than the federal approach. The court concluded that in an automobile accident case, the policy limits were not material and necessary in the prosecution of defense of such an action. The court found that defendant driver's license was discoverable; thus, the court denied the motion to vacate that portion of the notice.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to vacate the portion of plaintiffs' discovery notice that sought to compel and the automobile liability insurance policy of defendant automobile owner; but denied the motion to vacate the notice that sought production of the driver's license of defendant driver.


HEADNOTES

Discovery and inspection -- operator's license and owner's insurance policy -- in automobile negligence action, plaintiffs may have discovery and inspection of operator's license but not of owner's liability policy.

In an automobile negligence action, plaintiffs are entitled to discovery and inspection of the operator's license, but not of the owner's liability insurance policy. The latter item may be useful to plaintiffs in discussing settlement, but it is not "material and necessary in the prosecution or defense" of the action (CPLR 3101).

 

2110 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Pollack v. MacOmbs Inwood Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


52 Misc. 2d 563; 276 N.Y.S.2d 455; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1271



November 30, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons set forth herein, the motion for summary judgment with respect to the second cause of action is disposed of to the extent that judgment is granted to defendants dismissing the second cause of action pursuant to CPLR 3212 (subds. [b] and [e]). In all other respects, the motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant filed a motion for summary judgment in his action against defendant landlord for wrongful eviction and wrongful taking of personal property. Moreover, the tenant sought tremble damages under N.Y. Real Prop. Law § 853.


OVERVIEW: The landlord peacefully evicted the tenant for non-payment of three months of rent. The tenant claimed that he paid the rent prior to the trial date, but the trial court still entered a default judgment against him. In his complaint, the tenant alleged that the landlord also received a warrant to remove the tenant's personal payment for non-payment even though the tenant had paid the rent. Additionally, the tenant maintained that his eviction was unlawful. The landlord contended that the tenant was a statutory tenant and therefore his remedies were limited to the remedies granted in the New York City Rent and Rehabilitation Law. The court held that summary judgment with respect to the tenant's cause of action for wrongful taking of property raised questions of fact and therefore it denied the tenant's motion for summary judgment. The court then granted summary judgment in favor of the landlord, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3212(b), (e), on the wrongful eviction count. The court held that causes of actions under N.Y. Real Prop. Acts Law § 853 applied only where a landlord used force to remove the tenant.
