OUTCOME: The court denied the tenant's motion for summary judgment with respect to his action for wrongful taking of personal property. However, the court granted summary judgment in favor of the landlord on the tenant's wrongful eviction claim.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- wrongful eviction -- damages -- triable issues are presented by statutory tenant's allegations that defendant landlord and defendant Marshal, acting under invalid warrant of dispossess, wrongfully removed tenant's belongings during his absence and lost or damaged $ 1,500 worth of furniture and clothing -- but changing locks on door did not give tenant cause of action for triple damages for forcible eviction or detainer (Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, § 853).

1. Triable issues are presented by the allegations of a statutory residential tenant that the defendants (the landlord and a New York City Marshal), proceeding under an improperly obtained and invalid warrant of dispossess, wrongfully removed the tenant's belongings during the tenant's absence, and that, in the course of such removal or in the course of defendants' placing said [***2] belongings in storage, $ 1,500 worth of the tenant's furniture and clothing were broken, lost or stolen.

2. However, the fact that the defendants changed the locks on the door does not give plaintiff a cause of action for treble damages for "forcible entry or detainer" by "fear of personal violence" (Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, § 853). Plaintiff's further allegations that the defendants "threatened a breach of the peace should plaintiff attempt to re-enter said apartment, and since then have held and still hold forcible possession of said apartment, and hold and keep plaintiff out of said apartment by force or by putting him in fear of personal violence" are merely conclusory. This cause of action is dismissed.

 

2111 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Barrett v. Cuskelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


52 Misc. 2d 250; 275 N.Y.S.2d 280; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1304



November 21, 1966 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought an action against defendant, the Board of Fire Commissioners, to set aside a special election of voters in a fire district in which a referendum was approved authorizing the improvement of a firehouse and the issuance of bonds to pay for the costs. The Board filed a motion for summary judgment, and the taxpayers filed a cross motion.


OVERVIEW: The Board adopted a resolution authorizing the project and directing that a special election be held to submit the proposition to the voters. Notice of the election was published in a weekly newspaper and posted in five places throughout the fire district. In granting the Board's motion, the court held that the taxpayers presented no satisfactory evidence in support of its causes of action that attacked the manner in which the election was conducted and that the first two causes of action, relating to the publication of the notice, were legally insufficient. No proof was submitted to show that ballots were cast by unqualified voters, and there was no contradiction of the Board's affidavit that none of the voters were challenged. A screened off area provided for marking of the ballots afforded sufficient privacy to insure secrecy. The court also examined the notice of election and found its contents gave clear and precise information of the time and place of the election. Finally, the court held that the weekly newspaper met the requirements of N.Y. Town Law § 264 as it was circulated throughout the entire area in which it was intended that that the notice be read.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Board's motion and denied the taxpayer's cross motion.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- fire district -- fire district's Board of Fire Commissioners resolved to build addition to firehouse and issue $ 130,000 bonds therefor; clear notice of referendum was properly posted and published, and election was properly conducted; taxpayers' action to set aside voters' approval dismissed (Town Law, §§ 175, 179; Local Finance Law, § 38.00) -- general weekly newspaper published in district has "a general circulation in the district" (Town Law, § 175), though circulation is only 5,000.

The Board of Fire Commissioners of the Levittown Fire District duly resolved to construct and equip an addition to a firehouse and to issue bonds therefor not exceeding $ 130,000, and to submit such proposition to a referendum or special election. Notice was published once in the Levittown Tribune, a weekly newspaper. Although this newspaper had a circulation of only 5,000 in a district of 15,000 qualified voters, it had "a general circulation in the district" (Town Law, § 175). The balloting place was sufficiently private. There is no sufficient proof that any unqualified voters cast any ballots. The proposition was properly approved at this special election,  [***2] by a vote of 75 to 17 (Town Law, § 179). The Local Finance Law ( § 38.00) does not require a Board of Fire Commissioners to give public notice of the meeting at which the board adopts a resolution to conduct such a referendum. A taxpayers' action to set aside the referendum and the voters' approval of the proposition is dismissed.

 

2112 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ten West 28th Street Realty Corp. v. Moerdler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


52 Misc. 2d 109; 275 N.Y.S.2d 144; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1315



November 17, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application is, accordingly, denied and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, pursuant to N.Y. Mult. Dwell. Law § 302-a, petitioner landlord challenged the validity of certain orders promulgated by respondent Commissioner of Housing and Buildings of the City of New York and sought judgment vacating and annulling the orders as arbitrary, capricious, and contrary to law.


OVERVIEW: Under § 302-a, the Commissioner was empowered to promulgate a list classifying certain violations of the law as "rent impairing." Under § 302-a, when a rent impairing violation occurred and was not properly remedied, tenants could withhold rent from the landlord. The landlord challenged the validity of 25 of the listed violations as arbitrary and capricious. The landlord also challenged the constitutionality of § 302-a, urging that the sanctioned withholding of rents by tenants while they enjoyed the use of property was a denial of property without due process of law. In dismissing the petition, the court held that § 302-a was a constitutional exercise of the state's police powers. It was a means to induce owners of multiple dwellings to maintain and repair the properties. In order to promote the public interest in the maintenance of safe and sanitary housing accommodations, the legislature was warranted in exercising its police powers. Further, the legislation was addressed to a legitimate end and the measures taken were reasonable and appropriate to secure that end. It could not be said that the Commissioner's determination was arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition and denied the application.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- abatement of rent -- multiple dwellings in New York City -- statute abating rent in case of serious violations -- pursuant to constitutional statute (Multiple Dwelling Law, § 302-a), New York City Commissioner of Housing and Buildings held public hearings and validly and reasonably promulgated list of 57 serious violations which, if not remedied after Commissioner's six months' notice, may be asserted by tenants as defenses to rent nonpayment dispossess proceedings.

The Multiple Dwelling Law ( § 302-a) provides that the city's Commissioner of Housing and Buildings may promulgate a list of conditions in multiple dwellings which constitute a serious threat to the life, health or safety of the occupants, and may give the owner of such a building six months to correct such conditions, and that thereafter a tenant may defend a rent nonpayment dispossess proceeding by depositing the rent in court and pleading the landlord's noncompliance with the Commissioner's notice, and that the landlord will be deprived of the rents if it is found on the trial that the conditions have gone unremedied,  [***2] unless it is found that the conditions were caused by the tenant or the tenant's family or his guests or invitees. As prescribed by said section, the Commissioner held public hearings and promulgated a list of 57 such conditions, all of them reasonably related to the evils to be remedied. The statute is constitutional and the list is rational. Review proceeding ( CPLR, art. 78) is dismissed.

 

2113 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Pierce v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


52 Misc. 2d 10; 274 N.Y.S.2d 959; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1350



November 4, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiff's cross motion for a judgment declaring plaintiff is not subject to the New York State Sales and Compensating Use Taxes (Tax Law, arts. 28, 29) is granted; articles 28 and 29 of the Tax Law are unconstitutional, illegal and invalid as applied to plaintiff, and defendant and its officers are restrained from enforcing the said Tax Law in connection with the plaintiff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court were the parties' cross-motions for summary judgment. Defendant, the New York State Tax Commission, filed a motion under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3212 for summary judgment to the effect that plaintiff taxpayer was subjected to N.Y. Tax Law art. 28, 29 and that the statutes were valid and constitutional. The taxpayer filed a cross-motion for a judgment declaring that he was not subject to the New York State Sales and Compensating Use Taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a North American Indian in tribal relations, member of the Onondaga Nation. He owned a gift shop located on the Onondaga Indian Reservation in which he sold articles made by tribal members living on the Reservation. The Commission had required the taxpayer to file a certain form with the State Department of Taxation and Finance under the state sales and compensating use tax law. The taxpayer refused to file the form, to collect the tax from his customers, or to pay to the department the taxes claimed to be due on sales made at his place of business. The Commission and the Department were enforcing the New York State Sales and Compensating Use Taxes on the taxpayer and others of similar status. The court held that N.Y. Tax Law arts. 28, 29 were unconstitutional, illegal, and invalid as applied to the taxpayer. The taxes would place on tribal Native Americans within a reservation the multiple burdens of taxpayer, tax collector, accountant, and fiduciary, burdens which could well be in addition to those which the tribe or Congress could prescribe and thereby disturb and disarrange activities taking place on a reservation under the protection of the federal government.


OUTCOME: The court granted the taxpayer's cross-motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- State sales tax -- State sales tax and use tax cannot constitutionally be applied to Onondaga Indian who resides on Reservation and maintains gift shop there in which he sells articles made by other tribal residents.

The New York State sales taxes and compensating use taxes (Tax Law, arts. 28, 29) cannot constitutionally be applied to a member of the Onondaga Nation (one of the Six Nations Iroquois Confederacy duly recognized by the United States Government) who resides on the Onondaga Reservation near Syracuse and who owns a gift shop on the Reservation in which he sells articles and souvenirs made by other tribal Indians who, like him, live in tribal relations on the Reservation and maintain their tribal integrity there (U. S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl. 3). The Indian Law ( § 5) opens [***2] State courts to Indians who wish to use them; it does not oust the Council of Chiefs of the Onondaga Nation.

 

2114 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gomillion v. State


Claim No. 43467


Court of Claims of New York


51 Misc. 2d 952; 274 N.Y.S.2d 381; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1357



November 3, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion of the State of New York to dismiss this claim is granted, and claimant's motion for summary judgment is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the State of New York (state), filed a motion to dismiss claimant former inmate's false imprisonment claim. The inmate filed a cross-motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Within a year after his release from a mental institution, the inmate was arrested and charged with a felony. The inmate was returned to the institution and, thereafter, was transferred to a state hospital where he spent approximately seven years before being returned to the institution where he was later released under outpatient care. The inmate filed a claim against the state alleging false imprisonment for the time he spent in the state hospital. The court granted the state's motion to dismiss pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211 and denied the inmate's motion for summary judgment. The court found that it was unable to determine whether the inmate's claim was time-barred because it did not have sufficient evidence to determine whether the inmate fell within the tolling provisions of N.Y. C.P.L.R. 208 after his release from the institution on outpatient care. Nonetheless, the court held that the inmate failed to state a cause of action because his transfer to the state hospital was authorized under N.Y. Correct. Laws § 412. Further, the inmate was not deprived of his freedom by the transfer because he was already committed to the institution and had not objected to the commitment.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion to dismiss the inmate's false imprisonment claim and denied the inmate's motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

False imprisonment -- transfer to Matteawan State Hospital -- since former inmate of Matteawan State Hospital was validly transferred from State hospital to Matteawan State Hospital (Correction Law, former § 412), he has no claim against State for false imprisonment.

On two occasions, claimant was incarcerated at Matteawan State Hospital. Thereafter, by an order of County Court, he was admitted to Hudson River State Hospital. He was released from the latter hospital, and, about a year later, he was arrested and charged with a felony. He was then returned to Hudson River State Hospital. Three years later, by an order of the State Commissioner of Mental Hygiene, he was transferred to Matteawan State Hospital (Correction Law, former § 412). After seven years, he was returned to Hudson River State Hospital. From there, two years later, he was released under outpatient care. Much more than 90 days thereafter (Court of Claims Act, § 10, subd. 3), he filed a claim against the State for unlawful transfer to, and hence false imprisonment [***2] at, Matteawan. It is unnecessary to determine whether he was still under such mental disability as would extend said 90-day statute (cf. CPLR 208). He was incarcerated at Matteawan State Hospital pursuant to an official order which was valid and lawful during the period of his incarceration; and hence he has no claim against the State.

 

2115 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. McDonough


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


51 Misc. 2d 1065; 275 N.Y.S.2d 8; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1367



November 2, 1966 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court upon defendants' motion to reargue a decision of the court. The previous decision of the court denied certain relief and granted a hearing to determine the legality of various legal processes, including a wiretap order. The court ruled that the wiretap order and affidavit demonstrated the requisite reasonable grounds for the issuance of the said order.


OVERVIEW: The motion raised significant questions as to the extent of an attack on a judicially authorized wiretap order. The issue was raised because the wiretap order's supporting affidavit stated that the affiant received information from a member of a city police department. The affidavit further alleged that the informant did state that in compliance with a court authorized wiretap he heard the numbers dialed and that another party did answer the call. That the party calling did then relay to the answering party horse bets. Defendants sought to inquire into the legality of the city wiretap order. They contended that if the city wiretap order was illegal, then the fruits of that order were tainted and should not have been used to obtain the county wiretap order. The court noted that the affidavits in support of the instant motion lacked the necessary allegations to warrant a hearing on the ground of perjuriousness. However, in view of the holding that the court would review the legality of the city wiretap order, the product of which was the basis of the county wiretap order, the court directed that the prosecutor furnish it with a copy of the city wiretap order and supporting affidavit.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to reargue and upon reargument the original order was withdrawn and vacated.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- wiretap orders -- Nassau County ex parte order to tap telephone in Nassau County was obtained on basis, partly, of telephone call intercepted in New York County under New York County ex parte wiretap order; Nassau County Court directs Nassau County District Attorney to furnish counsel for indicted defendants with copies of supporting affidavits and orders issued in New York County and in Nassau County (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 813-a, 813-c) -- but court will not prohibit divulging of any intercepted telephonic communications -- statutes (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-c; § 177, subd. 1) constitutional -- hearing will be held on defendants' motion to suppress statements they made to law-enforcement authorities.

1. Pursuant to a New York County ex parte order, the New York City police tapped a telephone wire in New York County and heard, among other things, a telephone call to a telephone number in Nassau County which was answered by one "Charles" with whom the New York caller placed a bet on a horse race. Based partly on that information, the police in Nassau County obtained an ex parte order in Nassau County to tap the telephone of said "Charles" in Nassau County; and thereafter [***2] an indictment was obtained in Nassau County against "Charles" and another person. Said defendants have now moved in the Nassau County Court for an order to suppress any evidence obtained by wiretap, on the asserted ground that the affidavits in support of the wiretap orders did not show any "reasonable grounds" for the orders (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 813-a, 813-c; U.S. Const., 4th Amdt.). In connection with that motion, the Nassau County Court directs the Nassau County District Attorney to furnish defendants' counsel with a copy of both the New York County and the Nassau County wiretap orders and supporting affidavits. If the New York County order was issued without "reasonable grounds", any evidence obtained pursuant to it cannot legally support the Nassau County order authorizing a tap of the telephone of defendant "Charles". Moreover, the defendants are entitled to examine said supporting affidavits and to controvert specifically, if they can, any specifically false or perjurious statements therein -- in which event the defendants may be entitled to a hearing on their motion.

2. The court will not issue an order prohibiting any persons from divulging any intercepted telephonic [***3] communications.

3. Section 813-c and section 177 (subd. 1) of the Code of Criminal Procedure are constitutional.

4. Immediately preceding defendants' trial, a hearing will be held on defendants' motion to suppress any statements which they made to law-enforcement authorities.

Niagara Frontier Milk Distributors Bargaining Agency, Inc. v. Wickham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


51 Misc. 2d 885; 274 N.Y.S.2d 299; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1374



October 31, 1966 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner milk distributors filed an application for an order declaring an action by respondent, the Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets of the State of New York, null and void upon the ground that the basis for the Commissioner's action in amending an order governing the operation of the distributors resulted in an unconstitutional delegation of administrative powers.


OVERVIEW: An administrative order issued by the Commissioner regulated the handling of milk in certain counties. The Commissioner amended the order to provide that the price for certain milk be the higher of either a specified amount or the price established for the New York-New Jersey Milk Marketing Area. The distributors asserted that this action was null and void because the amendment resulted in an unconstitutional delegation of administrative powers in that the formula proposed for setting the prices unlawfully vested price-fixing powers given to the Commissioner in the Secretary of Agriculture of the United States. Although N.Y. Const. art. III, § 1 prohibited the delegation of legislative power by an administrative agency, the court held that the amended order did not unconstitutionally delegate the Commissioner's power. The formula merely related to the ultimate determination of a price which was used as an economic factor to establish the variable in the amended order. This factor could have been relied upon by the Commissioner in the formulating of his regulating plan within constitutional limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commissioner's action in amending the order.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Agriculture -- milk marketing orders -- Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets validly fixed price of Class I milk in Niagara Frontier area at Class I-A price in New York-New Jersey area ( 1 NYCRR Parts 20, 21); this did not delegate legislative power (N. Y. Const., art. III, § 1) to United States Secretary of Agriculture.

Pursuant to the Agriculture and Markets Law (art. 21, § 258-m), the New York State Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets properly and validly amended his Niagara Frontier Milk Marketing Area Official Order No. 127 ( 1 NYCRR Part 21), subject to certain adjustments, so as to fix the price of Class I milk for the months of June through December of 1966 at the higher of $ 6.20 per hundredweight or the Class I-A price established for the New York-New Jersey Milk Marketing Area by his Official Order No. 126 ( 1 NYCRR Part 20). The amendment did not delegate legislative powers (N. Y. Const., art. III, § 1) to the United States Secretary of Agriculture; rather, the amendment properly reflected the economic effect of prices in one area upon prices in another area.

 

2117 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hama Realty Co. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


52 Misc. 2d 192; 274 N.Y.S.2d 392; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1431



October 14, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The plaintiff's motion is denied, and the cross motions are granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross motions for summary judgment were filed in plaintiff taxpayer's action against defendants, a city and a law school, alleging that an auction sale by the city at which the law school was the successful bidder violated the city charter and the state constitution and that because a portion of the property sold would be used for educational purposes, it would be exempt from taxation.


OVERVIEW: At an auction, the city sold property to the law school. The taxpayer filed an action alleging that the sale violated the city charter and the state constitution and that because a portion of the property sold would be used for educational purposes, it was exempt from taxation, thereby increasing the taxes of the taxpayer. Cross motions for summary judgment were filed, and the State Attorney-General was permitted to intervene. The court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and held that all auction sales of real property by the city to nonprofit corporations organized for educational and other purposes was expressly authorized by 1966 N.Y. Laws 584. Further, because the sale was at an auction, any qualified purchaser deeming the property more valuable than the amount bid by the law school could have put in a higher bid. The city had the right to restrict the sale to certain types of bidders, and the fact that some of the property would be exempt from real estate taxation because used for educational purposes did not invalidate the sale.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- sale of real property -- auction sales -- sale at auction by City of New York to Brooklyn Law School of property which formerly housed Supreme Court was valid (Administrative Code of City of New York, § D51-66.10) -- plaintiff failed to establish that sale is invalid as gift of difference between value of property and amount bid by law school -- objection to constitutionality of validating statute as one aiding religious corporations without merit in connection with sale to Brooklyn Law School -- that some of property would be tax-exempt does not invalidate sale -- cause of action based on threatened eviction of one not party to action is without merit in taxpayer's suit.

1. The sale at auction by the City of New York to Brooklyn Law School of property which formerly housed the Supreme Court was not invalid under the City Charter. Such sales are expressly validated by chapter 584 of the Laws of 1966 (Administrative Code of City of New York, § D51-66.10) and such statute is constitutional, though retroactive, absent a vested interest adversely affected by such retroactivity.

 [***2] 2. Plaintiff failed to establish invalidity under the State Constitution as a gift of the difference between the value of the property and the amount bid by Brooklyn Law School. The test of whether a gift was involved is whether the value of the property under the restricted terms of sale exceeded the sale price. This was not shown. Moreover, the restrictions were proper ones and any qualified purchaser could have put in a higher bid than did the law school.

3. An objection to the constitutionality of the validating statute as one aiding religious corporations is not valid in connection with the sale to Brooklyn Law School.

4. The fact that some of the property would be tax-exempt because used for educational or similar purposes does not invalidate the sale.

5. A cause of action based on threatened eviction of one not a party to the action is without merit for plaintiff in this taxpayer's suit.

6. Plaintiff's motion for summary judgment is denied and cross motions for summary judgment are granted.

Moskowitz v. Board of Elections


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


51 Misc. 2d 827; 274 N.Y.S.2d 93; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1472



October 5, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application is denied and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prospective candidate for U.S. Congress, sought an order directing respondent, the Board of Elections of the City of New York, N.Y., and the Board Commissioner, to accept signatures obtained by the candidate after the final date for the filing of the independent nominating petitions.


OVERVIEW: The candidate filed a petition seeking to compel the Board and the Commissioner to accept signatures after the final filing date of the independent nominating petitions. The candidate was required under N.Y. Elec. Law § 314, subd. 19, to obtain 3,000 signatures in order to have his name placed on the ballot as a candidate of the officer of Representative in the U.S. Congress for the 19th Congressional District. The candidate claimed that as an orthodox observer of the Jewish Sabbath, eight of the 42 day period for collection of signatures were unavailable to him. The court noted that while eight days may have been unavailable to the candidate, the candidate was able to collect only 99 signatures in the 32 days in which the candidate did work to collect names. The court also rejected the candidate's contention that N.Y. Elec. Law § 136, subd. 2, was unconstitutional because it required an independent candidate to collect 3,000 signatures while requiring a party candidate to obtain only 750 signatures. The court held that it was up to the state legislature to amend the election law to give an "independent group" the same status as a "political party."


OUTCOME: The court denied the requested relief.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- independent nominating petitions -- court has no power to extend, because of religious holidays, 42 days' time within which to obtain signatures -- not unconstitutional to require 3,000 signatures on independent nominating petition and only 750 signatures on party designating petition.

1. For the general elections of November, 1966, signatures on independent nominating petitions may be obtained beginning on August 10, 1966 and the petition must be filed 42 days later, by September 21, 1966 (Election Law, § 138, subd. 7; § 314, subd. 19). The court has no power to extend this time because of Jewish or other religious holidays.

2. A designating petition for a party candidate for Congress requires only 750 signatures in New York City, whereas an independent nominating petition requires 3,000 signatures (Election Law, § 136, subd. 2, par. [d]; § 138, subd. 5, par. [c], cl. [4]); but the difference does not render the more difficult requirement unconstitutional.

 

2119 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


State by Lefkowitz v. ITM, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


52 Misc. 2d 39; 275 N.Y.S.2d 303; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1486; 3 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 775



September 29, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The relief requested by the petitioner for an injunction to effectuate the prevention of such fraudulent and illegal practices by any of the respondents is granted and the State of New York is awarded, pursuant to CPLR 8303 (subd. [a], par. 6), costs of $ 2,000 against respondent Rubin Sterngass, and the sum of $ 500 costs as against each of the respondents, Joseph Granda and Joseph D'Agostino.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Attorney General of the State of New York brought a special proceeding charging respondents, two domestic corporations, the sole shareholder, the president, sales manager, and three salesmen, with engaging in fraudulent and illegal practices in violation of N.Y. Exec. Law § 63(12), and sought an order enjoining, restraining, and prohibiting them from further engaging in such practices.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General charged two corporations and their officers and employees with violating N.Y. Exec. Law § 63(12) in their business selling appliances by a sales method known as a referral-sales program. The court granted the relief requested by the Attorney Generally, holding that: (1) the Attorney General proved all the fraudulent practices alleged in the petition; (2) the corporations repeatedly and persistently violated N.Y. Pers. Prop. Law § 402(2); (3) the contracts were unconscionable within the meaning of N.Y. U.C.C. Law and N.Y. Exec. Law § 63(12) and were unenforceable; (4) the corporations were guilty of persistent illegal acts in conducting a lottery, and all contracts were utterly void. The court also found that the sole shareholder and sales manager were guilty of persistently transacting business through an unlicensed foreign corporation. The injunction requested was granted to effectuate the prevention of such fraudulent and illegal practices. The state was awarded costs pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 8303(a)(6). The court found that most, if not all, of the representations made by the corporations and their employees to consumers were not true.


OUTCOME: The relief requested by the Attorney General for an injunction to effectuate the prevention of fraudulent and illegal practices by corporations and their officers and employees was granted. The state was awarded costs.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- fraudulent sales -- Attorney-General is granted permanent injunction (Executive Law, § 63, subd. 12) against sales of broilers, vacuum cleaners and television sets at unconscionable prices by means of fraudulent agreements promising purchasers commissions for referring sellers to other prospects -- such retail installment purchase contracts are declared unenforcible for violations of Personal Property Law ( § 402, subd. 2; § 403, subd. 3, last ununumbered par.) and as lotteries and nuisances (Penal Law, §§ 1370, 1371; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 9) and as made through unlicensed foreign corporation and unlicensed sales finance company (Business Corporation Law, § 1312; Banking Law, § 492) -- Executive Law ( § 63, subd. 12) is constitutional -- attack on Attorney-General's  [***2] good faith is made in bad faith -- $ 2,000 additional costs ( CPLR 8303, subd. [a], par. 6).

1. By means of "persistent fraud" and "illegality" (Executive Law, § 63, subd. 12) the respondents (two domestic corporations, their sole stockholder, their president, their sales manager, and three of their salesmen) induced many consumers to sign three-year retail installment contracts to purchase the following items: (a) an ordinary kitchen broiler which cost the respondents $ 80; time price $ 658.08; (b) another ordinary kitchen broiler which cost the respondents $ 120; time price $ 910.08; (c) an ordinary vacuum cleaner which cost the respondents $ 140; time price $ 920.52; and (d) a color television set which, on the average, cost respondents $ 450; time price $ 1292.40, or, if installed, up to $ 1575. These contracts are unconscionable and shall not be enforced (Uniform Commercial Code, § 2-302).

2. Besides falsely representing themselves and their products, the respondents induced their purchasers to sign purported agreements to earn commissions by referring respondents to other customers, and respondents fraudulently represented that their purchasers would earn, by means of [***3] an endless chain of referrals which was mathematically and realistically impossible, much more in commissions than their agreed purchase price and thus would never have to pay for their own purchases. This scheme constituted a lottery, a nuisance, and an illegal business (Penal Law, §§ 1370, 1371; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 9; Executive Law, § 63, subd. 12).

3. These contracts are unenforcible since made in violation of the Retail Instalment Sales Act (Personal Property Law, § 401 et seq.). In violation of section 402 (subd. 2) of said law, the respondents in each case made separate documents of the simultaneously executed retail installment purchase contract, the commission agreement, and the installation order which provided for a 20% penalty if the consumer cancelled prior to delivery; and then, in violation of section 403 (subd. 3, last unnumbered par.) of said law, the respondents assigned only the retail installment purchase contracts to finance companies and thereby aided the finance companies to claim that since they did not know of the commission agreements which provided for performance for a period greater than 10 days, they were not subject to the purchasers' defenses [***4] arising out of the sellers' nonperformance. Chapter 872 of the Laws of 1965 added to the aforesaid section 402 (subd. 2) a specific provision that any promises to the purchaser to compensate him for referrals must be contained in the retail installment contract; but this was merely declarative of the already existing law as construed by the courts.

4. Two of the respondents also illegally transacted business through an unlicensed Connecticut corporation (Business Corporation Law, § 1301, subd. [a]; § 1312), and through an identical trade name which was filed in Connecticut but for which no license was ever filed in New York, and through another domestic corporation which was not licensed as a sales finance company (Banking Law, § 491, subd. 7; § 492). These contracts are unenforcible.

5. Accordingly, respondents are permanently enjoined from "the continuance of such business activity" and such "fraudulent or illegal acts" and such "unconscionable contractual provisions" (Executive Law, § 63, subd. 12) and from aiding any others, through respondents' agents or attorneys, in enforcing such contracts.

6. Subdivision 12 of section 63 of the Executive Law is constitutional and [***5] valid.

7. The respondents' attack on the Attorney-General's good faith in prosecuting them is made in bad faith.

8. Pursuant to CPLR 8303 (subd. [a], par. 6), the Attorney-General is awarded $ 2,000 costs against one respondent and $ 500 costs against each of two other respondents.

Saratoga Harness Racing Ass'n v. Agric. & New York State Horse Breeding Dev. Fund


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


51 Misc. 2d 591; 273 N.Y.S.2d 611; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1542



September 10, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiff's motion for summary judgment is denied. Defendant's motion for summary judgment is granted to the extent of the difference between $ 45,222.89 and $ 20,516.06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 3212, plaintiff racing association filed a motion for a summary judgment in an action to retain breakage collected during a pari-mutuel betting season. Defendant Agriculture and New York State Horse Breeding Development Fund filed a cross motion for a summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 3212, the racing association filed a motion for a summary judgment in an action to retain breakage collected during a pari-mutuel betting season. The racing association contended that 1965 N.Y. Laws 567 was unconstitutional in that it enabled the Fund to derive income from pari-mutuel betting in violation of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 9. The Fund filed a cross-motion for a summary judgment asserting a right to collect its statutory 25 percent of the breakage accrued at the racing association's track. On consideration, the court denied the racing association's motion for a summary judgment and granted the Fund's motion for a summary judgment. The court held that the Fund's collection of its statutory percent of the breakage on pari-mutuel betting was constitutional because the Fund's activities were sufficiently allied with the original intent of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 9 as to further its purposes. By providing for the Fund and its activities, the State was protecting its source of revenue for the support of government.


OUTCOME: The court denied the racing association's motion for a summary judgment and granted the Fund's motion for a summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Horse racing -- Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law -- amendatory act creating Agriculture and New York State Horse Breeding Development Fund is constitutional -- act took effect at once, even though Governor did not appoint trustees under act until half year later, hence Fund is entitled to percentage of sums collected by harness racing associations during said half year.

1. The act creating the Agriculture and New York State Horse Breeding Development Fund, a public benefit corporation (L. 1965, ch. 567), is a valid amendment to the Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law (L. 1940, ch. 254, as amd.), "from which the state shall derive a reasonable revenue for the support of government" (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 9, subd. 1).

2. The act took effect immediately, July 7, 1965, even though the Governor did not appoint trustees under said act until after January 1, 1966. Accordingly, under the act, the Fund is entitled to $ 45,222.89 as its share of sums which the Saratoga Harness Racing Association, Inc., collected between July [***2] 7, 1965 and January 1, 1966. However, under the act, said harness racing association may be entitled to deduct from said sum $ 20,516.06 as its contribution to the purses for six stake races for New York bred horses.

Cypress Estates, Inc. v. Moore


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


51 Misc. 2d 463; 273 N.Y.S.2d 509; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1559



August 31, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment is granted declaring plaintiff's right to installation by it of individual sewage disposal facilities as first submitted and approved, and the disability on the part of the defendants to instead require a communal system.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to declare defendants', County Board of Health and Department of Health, resolution that no subdivision of 100 homes or more would be approved at all unless it provided for the installation of a communal sewage and treatment system unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The developer obtained approval for the installation of individual (cesspool) sewerage systems for a proposed subdivision. The developer's subdivision plans were fully approved. However, subsequently, defendants granted conditional approval to the subdivision plan for one year based on the promulgation of a new resolution. The developer filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to declare defendants' resolution that no subdivision of 100 homes or more would be approved at all unless it provided for the installation of a communal sewage and treatment system unconstitutional. On consideration, the court granted a judgment declaring the developer's right to install individual sewage disposal facilities as first submitted and approved by defendants. The court held that, although defendants acted within a delegated area of responsibility, defendants' actions were unreasonable as applied to the developer based on the developer's vested right in the development of the subdivision. Defendants could not fully approve the developer's subdivision plan and then grant conditional approval for one year based on the promulgation of the new resolution.


OUTCOME: The court granted a judgment declaring the developer's right to install individual sewage disposal facilities as first submitted and approved by defendants.


HEADNOTES

Health -- cesspools in real estate subdivision -- judgment granted declaring that realty subdivision owner is entitled to install individual cesspool for each home to be built, as originally approved by Suffolk County Department of Health, despite subsequent general resolution of county's Board of Health requiring communal sewage and sewerage system in large developments.

Plaintiff corporation bought a large tract of land in Suffolk County, and its plans and subdivision map were approved by the town planning board, and the Suffolk County Department of Health approved the plan to install an individual cesspool for each home to be built. Subsequently, said Department of Health limited its approval to one year. Thereupon plaintiff filed its approved subdivision map in the County Clerk's office, and conveyed over 200 acres for public uses, and contracted with the local water authorities, and constructed model homes, and spent large sums. Meantime [***2] the Suffolk County Board of Health promulgated a general resolution that no plans for a subdivision for over 100 homes -- such as plaintiff's -- would be approved unless the plans provided for the installation of a communal sewage and sewarage treatment system. Thereafter, said Board of Health refused to renew or extend its one-year approval of plaintiff's proposed individual cesspools, and finally the board disapproved plaintiff's cesspool plan in toto. Plaintiff is granted judgment against the Suffolk County Board and Department of Health declaring that plaintiff is entitled to install individual cesspools as originally approved. (Public Health Law, §§ 347, 1116, 1117, 1119; Town Law, §§ 265-a, 277.)

 

2122 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


51 Misc. 2d 297; 273 N.Y.S.2d 239; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1585



August 18, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, for the reasons stated, the motions of the defendant and intervenor-defendants are denied, and the cross motion of the plaintiffs for summary judgment is in all respects granted, each without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Commissioner of Education of the State of New York, and intervenor-defendants, parents of children who attended private schools, sought declaratory relief or to dismiss the complaint of plaintiffs, local Boards of Education, who alleged that an amendment to N.Y. Educ. Law § 701(2) (1965) regarding school books was unconstitutional and sought injunctive relief. The Boards made a cross-motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner and parents also sought a declaration that the amendment was constitutional. The amendment made by 1965 N.Y. Laws ch. 320 to N.Y. Educ. Law § 701(2) required the Boards to provide loans of school books to all students in grades 7 through 12, including those attending private or parochial schools. The Commissioner claimed that the Boards lacked standing, and the court ruled that the duties of the Boards as provided by N.Y. Const. art. XI, §1, N.Y. Educ. Law §§ 2(14), 305(2), allowed them to maintain the action on behalf of themselves and taxpayers. The court found that N.Y. Const. art. XI, § 3, did not permit the direct or indirect use of school funds in aid or maintenance of any school wholly or in part under the control of a religious institution, that the amendment was unconstitutional because the Court of Appeals of New York had specifically rejected the "child benefit theory" of funding the purchase of schoolbooks for parochial schools, and that the amendment violated both the Free Exercise and Establishment Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. 1. The court denied the motions to dismiss and granted summary judgment for the Boards.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment in favor of the Boards, and denied the motions of the Commissioner and the parents to dismiss the complaint or for a declaration that the amendment to the statute was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- school textbooks lending law -- statute providing that boards of education shall have power and duty to buy textbooks and lend them free to children attending private schools (Education Law, § 701, subd. 2, as amd. by L. 1965, ch. 320) is unconstitutional and void (N. Y. Const., art. XI, § 3; U. S. Const., 1st Amdt.) -- boards of education may maintain action for such declaratory judgment.

1. The provision of the Education Law ( § 701, subd. 2, as amd. by L. 1965, ch. 320) that "boards of education * * * shall have the power and duty to purchase and to loan upon individual request, to all children residing in such district who are enrolled in grades seven to twelve of a public or private school which complies with the compulsory education law, textbooks * * * which are designated for use in any * * * schools of the state or are approved by any boards of education * * * Such textbooks are to be loaned free", contravenes the provision of the [***2] New York State Constitution (art. XI, § 3) that "Neither the state nor any subdivision thereof shall use its property or credit or any public money, or authorize or permit either to be used, directly or indirectly, in aid or maintenance, other than for examination or inspection, of any school or institution of learning wholly or in part under the control or direction of any religious denomination, or in which any denominational tenet or doctrine is taught", and also contravenes the prohibition of the United States Constitution (1st Amdt., made applicable to the States by the 14th Amdt.) against any "law respecting an establishment of religion, or prohibiting the free exercise thereof"; and therefore the statute is void.

2. This action against the State Commissioner of Education for a declaratory judgment and injunction is properly brought by two boards of education. They have a right to invoke the constitutional function which the courts exercise in the balance of powers structure of our government to strike down an unconstitutional statute.

People ex rel. Dickie v. Nenna


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


51 Misc. 2d 343; 273 N.Y.S.2d 253; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1591



August 17, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the writ is dismissed and the relator ordered delivered to the custody of the agent of Maryland.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought a discharge from custody, which was brought by a writ of habeas corpus to test the legality of relator's detention pursuant to a warrant issued by the Governor of the State of New York on a requisition from the Governor of the State of Maryland demanding relator's extradition to that State to be tried for the crime of escape.


OVERVIEW: Relator, while serving a sentence in Maryland for larceny after trust, obtained an order determining him to be a "defective delinquent" and was committed to Patuxent Institution for confinement and treatment. When he continued to be confined after completion of his sentence, he escaped. The State of Maryland filed for extradition of relator for the crime of escape. Extradition was controlled by U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 2, as implemented by N.Y. Crim. Proc. § 829. Under § 829, the Governor of New York had a duty to arrest and deliver to the executive authority of any other State any person charged in that State with a crime and who had fled from justice. While commitment to the Institution as a defective delinquent was a civil proceeding, escape from that Institution was a crime under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 139.The court found that the guilt or innocence of relator subject to extradition was to be adjudicated in the demanding State.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and ordered that relator be delivered to the State of Maryland.


HEADNOTES

Extradition -- constitutionality of law of demanding State -- warrant of extradition must be complied with; test, if any, of constitutionality of demanding State's law must be had there, not here.

Relator was indicted and sentenced in the State of Maryland to two years' imprisonment, for larceny. Towards the expiration of his imprisonment, he was examined and adjudged to be a "defective delinquent * * * an actual danger to society" and was committed to Patuxent Institution for an indefinite period of confinement (Maryland Annotated Code, art. 31B). Although such an adjudication is a civil proceeding, both the State and Federal courts in Maryland have held that escaping from said institution is a crime as defined in the Maryland Annotated Code (art. 27, § 139). Relator escaped to New York after five years' commitment. The constitutionality of the Maryland statute may be tested in the Maryland courts, in the first instance, not in the New York courts. The Maryland Governor's warrant of extradition must be complied with. (U. S. Const., art. IV, § 2; cl. 2;  [***2] U. S. Code, tit. 18, § 3182; Uniform Criminal Extradition Act [Code Crim. Pro., § 827 et seq.].)

 

2124 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wheeler v. Islip


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


51 Misc. 2d 386; 273 N.Y.S.2d 399; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1597



August 16, 1966 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a condemnation proceeding brought by respondent town against a tract of land, which the town had designated as substandard and blighted, and the contemplated redevelopment of the land by respondent corporation in conjunction with the town's urban renewal plan. Petitioner argued that the redevelopment was not for a "public use" and challenged, inter alia, the selection of the corporation and the bidding process.


OVERVIEW: The town commenced condemnation proceedings against a tract of land, which it declared substandard and blighted. The town contemplated redevelopment of the area by the corporation as part of its urban renewal plan. The petitioner filed an action challenging the condemnation proceedings, arguing that the town had not complied with statutorily mandated procedures. The court dismissed the petition, holding that: 1) taking of the substandard property for redevelopment by the corporation was a recognized "public use;" 2) the town observed proper procedures in selecting the corporation; 3) the contract with the corporation complied with the state constitution and state law; 4) the town was not prohibited from exercising its eminent domain powers because the corporation would profit from the venture; 5) it was impossible to set a minimum price for conveyance of the land to the corporation prior to completion of the condemnation proceedings; 6) the town adhered to the requisite open bidding requirements; and 7) the contract provided for payment of condemnation awards without pledging the faith and credit of the town or violating the state constitution or statutory law.


OUTCOME: The actions of the town and all the steps taken in furtherance of the urban renewal project were confirmed and the proceeding was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- urban renewal -- town's urban renewal plan and contract lawful and proper; review proceeding dismissed on merits.

Condemnation by a town of a tract of 414 acres, consisting of 11 improved parcels and about 670 unimproved parcels, owned by 281 different owners, on the ground that the tract is substandard or insanitary (N. Y. Const., art. XVIII, § 1; General Municipal Law, arts. 15, 15-A), and for the purpose of then conveying the tract to a private corporation for the total amount of the condemnation awards plus all expenses incurred by the town, and which corporation has been properly designated by the town after proper advertising, bidding and hearing as the most "qualified and eligible sponsor" ( General Municipal Law, § 507) and which corporation has contracted with the town to improve and develop the tract in accordance with the town's duly adopted urban renewal plan, is lawful and proper, even though said corporation expects to find the enterprise profitable. The corporation has deposited $ 100,000 with the town as security for the performance of the contract, and has contracted to deposit with the town the moneys needed to pay the condemnation [***2] awards as the separate parcels are acquired. This method complies with section 16 of the Suffolk County Improvement Act (as amd. by L. 1945, ch. 746). Sections 150.00 and 151.00 of the Local Finance Law are inapplicable. The town is not making a gift of the land, nor is the town's credit being pledged (cf. N. Y. Const., art. VIII, § 1). Review proceeding ( CPLR, art. 78) is dismissed on the merits.

 

2125 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Garlin v. Murphy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


51 Misc. 2d 477; 273 N.Y.S.2d 374; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1598



August 16, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The determination of the respondents is confirmed and the petition is dismissed on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of a determination of respondent State Tax Commission that there was a deficiency due from him for personal income taxes for 1962, based on the holding that the taxpayer's undistributable shareholder's earnings was includable in his New York state adjusted gross income and taxable under N.Y. Tax Law § 612.


OVERVIEW: When the taxpayer filed his state income tax return, he omitted his proportionate share of the undistributed income of a corporation, which he had included on his federal income tax return. The taxpayer had previously made an election under subchapter S of chapter 1 of the Internal Revenue Code, 26 U.S.C.S. § 1371. N.Y. Tax Law 612(a) provided that the New York adjusted gross income of a resident individual meant his federal adjusted gross income as defined in the laws of the United States for the taxable year. The taxpayer claimed unconstitutionality, pointing to N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 3, which provided in part, that undistributed profits would not be taxed. The court found that the argument overlooked N.Y. Const. art. III, § 22, which went into effect on January 1, 1960, which required imposing taxes on income as defined by the laws of the United States. Because the year in question came after 1960, N.Y. Tax Law § 612a applied, and the undistributed income of the taxpayer's corporation was taxable by the state.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination and dismissed the petition on the merits.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- personal income tax -- stockholder of small business corporation which elected, for Federal tax purposes, that its undistributed profits be taxed not to itself but to its stockholders pro rata, must include his share of such undistributed profits in both his Federal and State income tax returns.

The New York State Constitution (art. XVI, § 3, last sentence) provides, since 1939, that "Undistributed profits shall not be taxed"; but since January 1, 1960 said Constitution (art. III, § 22) also provides that "Notwithstanding * * * any other provision of this constitution, the legislature, in any law imposing a tax or taxes on, in respect to or measured by income, may define the income on, in respect to or by which such tax or taxes are imposed or measured, by reference to any provision of the laws of the United States as the same may be or become effective at any time or from time to time". Accordingly, the Tax Law ( § 612, subd. [a]), effective as to income taxable years ending on and after December 31, 1960, validly provides that "The New York adjusted gross income [***2] of a resident individual means his federal adjusted gross income as defined in the laws of the United States for the taxable year". Petitioner owned stock in a so-called "subchapter S small business corporation" which elected (under U. S. Code, tit. 26, § 1371 et seq.), for Federal tax purposes, that its undistributed profits as of the close of the taxable year 1962 be included, not in its own taxable income, but in the taxable incomes of its stockholders pro rata. Petitioner's share of such undistributed profits was $ 8,279.97. He included this amount in his taxable income in his Federal income tax return, and he must likewise include this amount in his taxable income in his New York State income tax return. Our personal income Tax Law ( § 612, subd. [a]) is not rendered unconstitutional by the fact that the Federal corporation tax statute grants this deduction to the corporation while our corporation tax statute apparently does not; in any event, petitioner is not the corporation and cannot complain of this apparent unfairness.

 

2126 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cohen v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Bronx County


52 Misc. 2d 324; 275 N.Y.S.2d 719; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1625



August 3, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the foregoing reasons, the defendants' motions to dismiss the complaint are granted and plaintiff's motion for summary judgment is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parent, the father of two children attending public school, moved for summary judgment in his action against defendants, the State of New York, the City of New York, and others, for a judgment declaring N.Y. Educ. Law § 2553(2) unconstitutional. The statute provided the method for the selection of the New York City Board of Education. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. Educ. Law § 2553(2) provided for the selection of the members of the New York City Board of Education from nominations submitted to the mayor by a selection board. The parent argued that because the New York Education Law provided that other school districts could elect boards of education, the state had denied him the right to equal protection of the laws in violation of the federal and state constitutions. He further argued that such law had disenfranchised him and deprived him of rights and privileges received by other citizens in violation of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 1. The court held there was no violation of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 1 because the parent had shown no constitutional or statutory authority indicating that boards of education were to be elected. It found the legislature, under the plenary power granted by N.Y. Const. art. XI, § 1, had the right to provide for the selection of the New York City Board of Education in the manner set forth in N.Y. Educ. Law § 2553(2). It also found no equal protection violation. There were ample, reasonable bases for the establishment by the legislature of both elected and appointed boards of education in different areas of the state.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motions to dismiss the complaint and denied the parent's motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- election or selection of boards of education -- although voters of most school districts elect their boards of education, Legislature has validly provided that Mayor of City of New York shall fill vacancies in Board of Education of City of New York by appointments from among nominees submitted by selection board which is comprised of heads of various organizations.

The provision of the Education Law ( § 2553, subd. 2, as added by L. 1961, ch. 971), whereby the Mayor of the City of New York fills vacancies in the Board of Education of the City of New York by appointments from among nominees submitted by a selection board which is composed of heads of various organizations, is within the constitutional powers of the Legislature governing education. It is not an arbitrary and unreasonable classification for the Legislature to allow the boards of education to be elected directly by the voters of the common school districts and of the union free school districts and of the central school districts and of the city [***2] school districts in cities of less than 125,000 inhabitants and by the voters of the cities of Syracuse and Rochester, on the one hand, and only indirectly by the voters of the City of New York on the other hand. The statute does not arbitrarily and unreasonably discriminate against the voters of the City of New York or deprive them of any part of their elective franchise or of the equal protection of the laws. (N. Y. Const., art. I, §§ 1, 11; art. XI, § 1; U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.) This action by a New York City resident for a judgment declaring the statute unconstitutional is dismissed.

 

2127 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Griffith v. Krulewitch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


51 Misc. 2d 352; 273 N.Y.S.2d 168; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1631



August 1, 1966 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the application is dismissed and the petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner boxer sought review of a decision by respondent athletic commission pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 after the athletic commission determined that the boxer could hold only one championship boxing title at a time.


OVERVIEW: The boxer was welterweight champion of the world in boxing. The boxer signed a contract to fight for the middleweight championship of the world and, as part of the agreement, the parties adopted the athletic commission's rules. The applicant fought and won. The athletic commission determined that the applicant could hold only one championship boxing title at one time. The applicant sought review of the athletic commission's determination because the boxer claimed that the regulation against holding two titles was unconstitutional because it deprived him of his rights under the Fourteenth Amendment and the N.Y. Constitution. The court affirmed because the boxer had no vested property right to the title of welterweight champion of the world. Furthermore, the court determined that the athletic commission's action was not arbitrary or capricious.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed and denied the boxer's petition.


HEADNOTES

Prize fighting -- Rules of State Athletic Commission -- Rules of State Athletic Commission ( 19 NYCRR 218.6) reasonably and validly provide that holder of world championship in one class may enter and win world championship in another class but thereby forfeits his first title.

Pugilism and boxing are illegal in New York except as regulated by the New York State Athletic Commission ( Penal Law, §§ 1710- 1716; L. 1920, ch. 912; L. 1952, ch. 666). The rules of the commission (rule H, subd. 6 [in 19 NYCRR 218.6]) reasonably and validly provide: "No individual may hold a world's championship title in two or more classes at the same time, but the holder of one such championship title may enter a contest for the world championship title of another class. In the event that such individual wins such world's championship title in such other class, his original world championship is automatically vacated." Accordingly, when the world's welterweight boxing champion fought for and won the world's middleweight championship under the rules of the New York State Athletic Commission, he lost the welterweight championship.

 

2128 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Tully & Di Napoli, Inc. v. State


Claim No. 46282


Court of Claims of New York


51 Misc. 2d 11; 272 N.Y.S.2d 667; 1966 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1635



July 29, 1966 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state filed a motion for an order dismissing the claim of plaintiff subcontractor in an action by the subcontractor and plaintiff contractor for payment on a highway construction contract.


OVERVIEW: The contractor entered into a contract with the state for the construction of a highway. The contractor entered into a subcontract with the subcontractor for work on this highway. The contractor received state approval for the subcontract. The contractor and the subcontractor brought an action against the state. The court granted the state's motion to strike out the name of the subcontractor from the title of the claim. Any sums owed by the contractor to the subcontractor were to be determined based upon their liquidating agreement. There was no privity between the subcontractor and the state. The subcontractor had no right to sue as a third-party beneficiary of the contract. The state consented to be sued by the one with whom it has entered into the obligation of the contract. It owed nothing directly to the subcontractor, who was permitted to testify and who was the most competent witness concerning the portion of the contractor's claim involving his own work, under N. Y. Const., art. VI, § 9 and N.Y. Ct. Cl. Act § 9.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion to dismiss the claim of the subcontractor.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] State -- construction contracts -- subcontractor cannot join in contractor's claim against State, although contractor's claim should include items of subcontractor's claim (cf. N. Y. Const., art. VI, § 9; Court of Claims Act, § 9) -- but, pursuant to their agreement to accept judgment of Court of Claims, court will determine amounts owed by contractor to subcontractor -- court suggests that Court of Claims Act ( § 9) and Constitution be amended.

1. Although the State Department of Public Works often requires contractors to submit their subcontracts for the department's approval as to the competence of the subcontractors to perform the work, only the contractor can file a claim against the State. Such claim should properly include the items which the contractor owes the subcontractor, and the latter is probably the most competent witness as to his own portion of the work, but a dispute or lack of dispute between them is not a ground for allowing the subcontractor to be made a party to the contractor's claim against the State (cf. N. Y. Const., art. VI, § 9; Court of Claims Act, § 9). Accordingly, the subcontractor's name is stricken from the title of this claim and action.

 [***2] 2. However, this contractor and subcontractor have executed an agreement setting forth all the items claimed and agreeing to accept the judgment of the Court of Claims as a basis of liquidating their claims; accordingly, the court's judgment will state and determine the sums to be paid by this contractor to this subcontractor.

3. The court suggests that the statute be amended, and that, if necessary, a constitutional amendment be proposed at the forthcoming constitutional convention.
