The court concluded that (1) there was no issue of privilege against self incrimination; and (2) the duty imposed upon those employers described in the statute, namely to completely fill out and file the requisite Form LP-1, could not be disregarded, no matter how distasteful an employer found such mandated obligation.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Commissioner's petition for an order to compel compliance with an order and struck the employer's answer.


HEADNOTES

Labor -- improper practices by labor and management -- employer may not refuse to answer, in financial report form, question mandated by statute; relief must be sought from Legislature.

Respondent cannot avoid answering a question on a financial Employer Report Form (Labor Law, § 726, subd. 3, par. [d]), since no privilege against self incrimination is presented, merely because he objects to the requirement in the statute. The law must be obeyed. Respondent must seek redress from the Legislature to expunge paragraph (d) of subdivision 3 of section 726 of the Labor Law, whose provisions are incorporated into the question objected to by respondent. The duty imposed upon those employers described in the statute to fill out completely and file the requisite form may not be disregarded no matter how distasteful an employer may find such mandated obligation to be. The Industrial Commissioner is entitled to an order compelling respondent to answer the question.

 

2166 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Loos v. Redman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


48 Misc. 2d 592; 265 N.Y.S.2d 453; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1246



December 17, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Ordered, that said petition, in accordance with the foregoing memorandum of decision, be and the same is hereby denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, convicted of unlawful entry contrary to N.Y. Penal Law § 405, sought a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to imprisonment for one year, to pay a fine, and ordered to stand committed until the fine was paid, but no longer than one day for each dollar of the fine imposed. Petitioner alleged that the portion of his sentence that directed his imprisonment until the fine imposed was paid was for all intents and purposes, a sentence to confinement for an additional 16 1/2 months. Petitioner alleged that the distinction between a person who was able to pay the fine and one who was unable to do so, offended the Eighth Amendment. The court concluded that (1) a claim of unequal treatment would be presented whenever an indigent was confined in default of payment of a fine, whether that confinement was for even one day, completely aside from the fact that a longer term could have been imposed as punishment; and (2) sentences whether they imposed fines or terms of imprisonment, fell upon those convicted with unequal impact depending upon many factors.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sentence -- sentence of year in prison and $ 500 fine and directing confinement until fine is paid, but no longer than day for each dollar of fine, under statute permitting imprisonment for year and fine up to $ 500, not unconstitutional when imposed on indigent defendant (U. S. Const., 8th and 14th Amdts.; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 5).

Defendant was convicted of unlawful entry and sentenced to imprisonment for one year and to pay a $ 500 fine and ordered to stand committed until said fine was paid, but no longer than one day for each dollar of the fine, under a statute permitting imprisonment for not more than one year or a fine of not more than $ 500 or both (Penal Law, § 1937). It is not claimed that the prescribed punishment is excessive or unusual and it was not unlawful since the court had authority to pronounce it. The imprisonment which may follow upon failure to pay a fine is a means of coercing payment, not a punishment. The fact that defendant is indigent and unable to pay the fine does not render the sentence unconstitutional [***2] (U. S. Const., 8th and 14th Amdts.; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 5). Accordingly, defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus is denied.

 

2167 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bakery Salvage Corp. v. Lackawanna


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


48 Misc. 2d 975; 265 N.Y.S.2d 471; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1262



December 15, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment is granted to the plaintiff declaring this ordinance void and enjoining its enforcement; and to the defendant Town dismissing the City's cross claim, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought a declaratory judgment that defendant city's truck weight ordinance was unconstitutional and an injunction prohibiting the enforcement of the ordinance. Defendant town filed a cross-claim seeking the same relief as the company.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance limiting the weight of trucks operated within the city except for trucks making deliveries on Abbott Road. Abbott Road started in the city and dead-ended in the town. The company's plant was located on Abbott Road in the town. The only access to the plant was by taking one of the city's other streets to Abbott Road and driving through the city on Abbott Road. The effect of the ordinance would have been to halt all traffic to and from the plant. The company filed an action for a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutional, an injunction against enforcement, and to require the town to create access to the plant. The town filed a cross-claim against the city. The court held that the ordinance was void and enjoined its enforcement. The court held that an implied easement of necessary ingress and egress to an abutting public street arose unless the abutting owner had access to another adequate street. The denial of such an easement constituted the taking of property without due process of law. The court held that the city could exclude heavy trucks from certain streets, but there had to be adequate, safe and suitable alternative routes.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the company in its action for declaratory judgment and injunction against the city, declared the ordinance void, and enjoined enforcement of the ordinance.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- truck route in city and town -- city ordinance prohibiting trucks which weigh over five tons when loaded from using usual truck route, and which does not formally establish any truck routes, is adjudged void as to plaintiff factory located in adjoining town -- defendant city may not have judgment directing defendant town to establish truck route for plaintiff -- portion of this old road which lies within town was formerly county highway, but when State Thruway was cut through in 1957 and its barrier made cul-de-sac of this portion of road, county abandoned it and it reverted to town.

1. An old public road called Fisher Road begins, at one end, in the City of Lackawanna at the intersection of said road with another city street, and thence runs easterly 1,000 feet through a residential zone of the city to the dividing line between the city and the Town of West Seneca, and thence continues for 1,400 feet through a manufacturing zone of the town to the barrier of the New York [***2] State Thruway. Before the Thruway was built in 1957 through the town, Fisher Road continued further on and connected, at its other end, with an intersecting road in the town; but now Fisher Road ends at the Thruway barrier, like a cul-de-sac. Plaintiff's factory is in the town, on Fisher Road. Plaintiff makes toasted bread crumbs for dog food. Plaintiff uses trucks and tractor-trailers which weigh from 8 to 15 tons when loaded. Plaintiff could not remain in business economically if it were required to use smaller trucks. Yet the city has recently, in 1965, enacted an ordinance which prohibits trucks which weigh more than 5 tons gross from using Fisher Road, except when making deliveries -- meaning, of course, except when making deliveries on the part of Fisher Road which lies within the city. The city has not formally established any truck routes (cf. Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 1640). Fisher Road and its intersecting street in the city have been used for over 40 years as a truck route. The ordinance is aimed at plaintiff, and it unreasonably deprives plaintiff of property rights without compensation and without due process of law. Moreover, many of the town's own service [***3] trucks weigh more than 5 tons when loaded, and, in order to use Fisher Road, must first enter Fisher Road at its beginning point of intersection within the city. The court adjudges the ordinance void and enjoins the city from enforcing it.

2. The city's cross claim for a judgment directing defendant town to furnish a truck route for plaintiff and for other industries in the town (cf. Vehicle and Traffic Law, § 1660) is dismissed.

3. The portion of Fisher Road which lies within the town was formerly a county highway; but the court finds that, when the Thruway was built in 1957 and the Thruway barrier made a cul-de-sac of this portion of Fisher Road, the county abandoned this portion of Fisher Road and that thereupon this portion reverted to the town.

 

2168 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New York v. Social Service Employees Union


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


48 Misc. 2d 820; 266 N.Y.S.2d 277; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1286



December 9, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The city's motion as one for summary judgment is granted on the law dismissing the defendants' answers and defenses in the city's action and dismissing the unions' complaint in their action and the temporary restraint is vacated. The city's motion to dismiss the unions' complaint on the ground that they are not aggrieved (cf. Matter of Suffolk County Retail Wine & Liq. Dealers [New York State Liq. Auth.], 23 A D 2d 552) is denied in view of the consolidation of the actions, the unions being named as defendants in the city's action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated actions, plaintiff city sought summary judgment dismissing defendant unions' answers and defenses to the city's action to end a strike by public employees and dismissal of the unions' complaint seeking a determination of the constitutionality of the Condon-Wadlin Law, N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 108, which prohibited strikes by public employees, and an injunction against the enforcement of the penalty provisions of that Law.


OVERVIEW: The city brought an action against the unions, seeking to end a strike by city employees. The employees eventually returned to work and the unions brought suit to determine the constitutionality of the Condon-Wadlin Law, which condemned strikes by public employees, and to enjoin enforcement of its penalty provisions. The actions were consolidated and the court dismissed the unions' answers and defenses in the city's suit and dismissed the union's complaint. It determined that the Condon-Wadlin Law had already been declared constitutional and that the unions' main objection was a declaration of invalidity of the penalty provisions. It then found that there was no merit to the unions' argument distinguishing between economic and organizational or recognitional strikes and that there was no provision that accorded public employees the right of representation or collective bargaining. Finally, the Condon-Wadlin Law provided for notice and a public hearing on the imposition of a penalty and that any punishment for violating the law could be fixed only after notice and a hearing, with such punishment subject to judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the unions' answers and defenses in the city's action to end the strike. It also dismissed the unions' complaint and vacated the temporary restraint.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- strikes by public employees -- Condon-Wadlin Law ( Civil Service Law, § 108), prohibiting strikes by public employees, is constitutional -- penalty provisions of said law involve no question of due process, slavery, involuntary servitude, excessive fines or punishment, no defect, no infirmity.

1. An action by the City of New York against two labor unions and their officers, seeking to end a strike by the employees of the Welfare Department, and an action by the unions and their representatives against the city, seeking to determine the constitutionality of the Condon-Wadlin Law ( Civil Service Law, § 108), which condemns [***2] and prohibits strikes by public employees, and to enjoin enforcement of its penalty provisions, are consolidated, and a motion to dismiss the unions' complaint for failure to state a cause of action is treated as one for summary judgment.

2. The law already has been declared constitutional ( New York City Tr. Auth. v. Loos, 2 Misc 2d 733, affd. 3 A D 2d 740; Pruzan v. Board of Educ. of City of N. Y., 25 Misc 2d 945, direct app. on constitutionality dsmd. 9 N Y 2d 680, judgment affd. 12 A D 2d 923, affd. 9 N Y 2d 911). Economic and organizational or recognitional strikes are not distinguishable. There is no provision in law which accords to public employees rights of representation or collective bargaining. State and city employees are excluded directly from application of the State Labor Relations Act ( Labor Law, § 715, subd. [2]; § 721, subd. [3]).

3. With respect to the penalty provisions of the law, there is no question of due process, slavery, involuntary servitude, excessive fines or punishment, no defect, no infirmity. Any punishment forthcoming in individual cases may be fixed only after a hearing, subject to judicial review.

4. The city's motion as [***3] one for summary judgment is granted on the law, dismissing defendants' answers and defenses in the city's action and the unions' complaint, and a temporary restraint of enforcement for punishment of the strikers is vacated.

 

2169 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bookcase, Inc. v. Broderick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


49 Misc. 2d 351; 267 N.Y.S.2d 410; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1346



November 16, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The cross motion on behalf of the public officers is denied; and the plaintiffs may move for expeditious trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff booksellers, a retail store and its corporate president, sought a declaratory judgment adjudging invalid N.Y. Penal Law §§ 484-h, 484-i and enjoining the enforcement thereof by defendants, the city police commissioner, the county district attorney, and an individual who allegedly threatened to initiate further criminal proceedings. The booksellers sought temporary injunctive relief, and motions to dismiss were filed.


OVERVIEW: The challenged statutes prohibited the sale of sexually offensive literature to minors. The booksellers contended that it was unconstitutional to restrict the right to sell books on the basis of the age of the purchaser. The court dismissed the complaint against the individual, holding that a complaint against an individual could not be predicated upon an asserted violation of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV.As to the relief sought against the officials, the court observed that, to warrant the granting of a temporary injunction, the showing of a right to ultimate permanent relief had to be clear. A statute, however, was entitled to a presumption of regularity and validity, and laws for the protection of children's well-being were within the state's police power. Accordingly, the booksellers could not obtain a temporary injunction. The court denied the officials' motion to dismiss, stating that the booksellers were entitled to a forum to determine their claim of unconstitutionality without risking prosecution and that the use of the declaratory judgment procedure was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court granted the individual's motion to dismiss, denied the booksellers' request for a temporary injunction, and denied the officials' motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sale of book to minor -- action for declaratory judgment proper remedy to test validity of statutes forbidding sale of sexually offensive literature to minors (Penal Law, §§ 484-h, 484-i) -- motion for temporary injunction restraining enforcement of such statutes denied absent clear right to permanent relief -- complaint dismissed as to defendant clergyman whose opposition to sale of such material to minors apparently resulted in initiation of earlier prosecution against plaintiffs.

1. An action for a declaratory judgment is the proper remedy to test the validity of a statute. However, in such an action, there is a presumption of validity in favor of the questioned statutes, in this case sections 484-h and 484-i of the Penal Law, making criminal the sale to persons under 17 and 18 years of age, respectively, of sexually offensive literature. Moreover, the Court of Appeals has held that "a constitutionally valid statute defining obscenity in its impact on the young * * * might emerge under careful draftsmanship." ( People v. Kahan, 15 N Y 2d [***2] 311.) Accordingly, since plaintiffs have no clear right to ultimate permanent relief, their motion to temporarily restrain the Police Commissioner and the District Attorney from prosecuting them under said statutes is denied.

2. A motion by the Police Commissioner and the District Attorney for dismissal of the complaint is denied as plaintiffs are entitled to a forum to determine their claim of unconstitutionality without risking prosecution.

3. The complaint against defendant clergyman whose opposition to the sale of salacious material to minors apparently resulted in initiation of an earlier prosecution against plaintiffs is dismissed, as a complaint against an individual may not be predicated upon an asserted violation of the Fourteenth Amendment ( Civil Rights Cases, 109 U.S. 3, 11 [1883]).

 

2170 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. McMorran


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


48 Misc. 2d 79; 264 N.Y.S.2d 296; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1347



November 15, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner brought a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 against respondent state officials to compel payment of a sum, plus accrued interest, representing part of a condemnation award.


OVERVIEW: The state appropriated the property owner's hotel properties for highway purposes. The award included interest from the date of the filing of notice of appropriation and map to the date of the entry of judgment on the award. The property owner remained in possession of the premises and continued to operate the hotel enterprise for six months after he received notice of appropriation. After entry of judgment on the award, the state officials unilaterally withheld a sum as the fair rental value of the condemned property for the period that the property owner had possession after the notice of appropriation. The court observed that, although a condemnee was not allowed interest during periods when the condemnee had an equivalent use of the property, the burden of proof as to any amount sought to be offset was upon the state. The state officials, having failed to sustain that burden at trial, had no authority to withhold funds that were due and owing pursuant to a valid and binding judgment.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the property owner.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Eminent domain -- compensation -- since State failed to raise issue in Court of Claims that value of claimant's use and occupation should be deducted from interest on his award, owner is granted order of Supreme Court ( CPLR, art. 78) directing State officials to pay him interest which was included in Court of Claims judgment of award -- portion of Highway Law ( § 30, subd. 13-c) which permits State to withhold moneys due on award is not retroactive.

The owner of hotel properties was awarded $ 72,763.83 in condemnation, with interest from the date of filing of the map and notice of appropriation on March 23, 1964, when title vested in the State, to the date of entry of such judgment of award in the Court of Claims, January 12, 1965. He remained in profitable possession and operation of the hotel properties, until November 9, 1964. The State did not cause him to be summarily dispossessed; nor did the State make any agreement with him as to rent to be paid by him for use and occupation pending an award; nor did the State make any assertion in the Court of Claims as to the value of his use and occupation; nor did the State appeal from the judgment of the Court of Claims awarding [***2] him $ 72,763.83 (Highway Law, § 30, subds. 6, 12, 13-c). Said last-mentioned subdivision (Highway Law, § 30, subd. 13-c) became effective on April 22, 1964, after title had vested on March 23, 1964. The portion of said subdivision which permits the State to withhold moneys due on a judgment of award is not retroactive. Of course, even prior to said subdivision's enactment, the State could have asserted in the Court of Claims that the claimant owed the fair value of his use and occupation as an offset to any interest on the award; but the burden of so alleging and proving was on the State. The State's failure so to allege or prove cannot give it the right to attack the judgment collaterally. Accordingly, the owner is granted an order of the Supreme Court ( CPLR, art. 78) directing the State officials to pay him the balance of the sum awarded by the Court of Claims.

 

2171 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Feinberg


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


48 Misc. 2d 187; 264 N.Y.S.2d 424; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1392



October 29, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an action against defendant for failure to comply with a city building department order for the removal of a grocerette vending machine in the basement of an apartment house.


OVERVIEW: The city building department ordered defendant, who was the agent of an apartment house in a residential district, to discontinue use of a grocerette vending machine in the basement of the building. Defendant refused. The State filed an action against defendant for failure to comply with the order. Defendant argued that the vending machine was an accessory use under New York City, N.Y., Zoning Res. § 12-10. The court found defendant guilty and imposed a $ 10 fine because the building department's decision that the vending machine was not an accessory use, was not illegal on its face.


OUTCOME: The court found defendant guilty of failure to comply with a city building department order and imposed a $ 10 fine.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- order of Building Department to remove so-called "grocerette" coin-operated vending machine from basement of apartment house cannot be reviewed by Criminal Court; defendant did not appeal to city's Board of Standards and Appeals as to such asserted "accessory use" (N. Y. City Zoning Resolution, § 12-10); defendant is found guilty.

The New York City Building Department ordered defendant, agent of an apartment house, to discontinue the use of a so-called "grocerette", coin-operated vending machine, which was placed near a milk-vending machine in the basement of the apartment house. The "grocerette" dispensed bread, pies, doughnuts, eggs, and soda drinks. Apparently the Building Department had determined that the so-called "grocerette" was not one of the "accessory uses" permitted by the New York City Zoning Resolution (§ 12-10). Defendant did not appeal to the city's Board of Standards and Appeals (New York City Charter, § 666, subd. 6). He ignored the order at his peril. It is not for the Criminal Court of the City of New York to review a municipal order which is valid on its face. Defendant is found guilty and is fined $ 10.

 

2172 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Meyer v. Wiess


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Sullivan County


47 Misc. 2d 1056; 263 N.Y.S.2d 813; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1400



October 28, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed an action against defendants, county board and college board, seeking a declaration that the designated site for the community college was not valid without the county board's approval. The taxpayer filed a motion for summary judgment which the county board joined. The college board filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The college board sought a permanent site for the community college. The college board approved two different sites, but the county board rejected each of them. The college board sought to declare a permanent site without the approval of the county board. The taxpayer filed an action against the county board and the college board, seeking a declaration that the college board was not authorized to establish a permanent site for the community college without the approval of the county board. The taxpayer filed a motion for summary judgment and the college board filed a motion to dismiss. The court held that the consent and approval of the county board was necessary for the establishment of a permanent site for a community college. The taxpayer was entitled to a declaratory judgment to the effect that the proposed site was not the duly constituted site of the community college, and that no site could have been established without the approval of a majority of the county board.


OUTCOME: The court granted the taxpayer's motion for a summary declaratory judgment. The college board's motion to dismiss was denied.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Colleges and universities -- community colleges -- site for construction of community college cannot be established without approval of majority of County Board of Supervisors, even though college board has accepted individual's gift of land (Education Law, art. 126).

Under article 126 of the Education Law, the county is the local sponsor of a community college, and the County Board of Supervisors must appropriate moneys and levy taxes in order to pay half of the capital construction fund and a third of the annual operating expenses. Although the trustees of such community college may, by their own majority vote, accept a gift of land, in the form of a deed to the county as trustee for the college, from an individual who, in this instance, also offers to give the college $ 500,000 if the land is accepted as the site for the college, the County Board of Supervisors may, by a majority vote, reject the trustees' selection of that site (cf. Education Law, § 6306, subd. 4); that is, no site can be established without the approval of a majority of the County Board of Supervisors. Declaratory judgment is rendered accordingly.

 

2173 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Clute


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Washington County


47 Misc. 2d 1005; 263 N.Y.S.2d 826; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1410



October 26, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a Justice's Court of the Town of Kingsbury (New York), which convicted defendant, on the verdict of a jury, of a violation of the Zoning Ordinance of the Town of Kingsbury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's daughter had a fire at her home and wanted to live in a mobile home to be located in her mother's back yard. Defendant applied for an exception to the zoning ordinance, which did not allow mobile homes to be located anywhere except in a designated trailer park. The application was denied. Defendant allowed her daughter to park her mobile home in her back yard anyway and defendant was convicted of violating the town's zoning ordinance. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that defendant had violated the ordinance. Defendant was precluded from making a constitutional challenge to the ordinance because she failed to appeal to the Board of Appeals when her initial request was denied. The jury was properly allowed to take exhibits into its deliberations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for a violation of a zoning ordinance.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- jury properly found defendant guilty of violating zoning ordinance prohibiting even one trailer in residential zones unless in trailer parks -- after defendant was refused permit, she failed to apply to Zoning Board of Appeals; hence she cannot now assert that ordinance deprives her of property: in any event, ordinance is reasonable and constitutional -- trial court properly allowed jury to take all exhibits into jury room (Code Crim. Pro., § 425).

1. A zoning ordinance permitting trailers in (a) trailer parks and (b) agricultural districts, but (c) not in residential districts, bears a valid relation to the public health, safety, and general welfare, since only in trailer parks can the problems of water, sewage, waste disposal, etc., be adequately solved and supervised. On a farm, one isolated trailer may be permitted, since it is unlikely that its sewage will contaminate the water supply of the general area. But, in a residentially zoned district, even one isolated trailer is a danger to health and a detriment to land values. Defendant asked for a permit to place what she said would be a [***2] temporary trailer on her land for the benefit of her daughter who, she said, had lost the use of her own house because of a fire. Defendant's request was denied, but she brought in the trailer anyway. A jury found her guilty of violating the zoning ordinance and the judgment of conviction thereon is affirmed.

2. Since she did not apply to the Zoning Board of Appeals, she cannot assert that the ordinance unconstitutionally deprives her of all reasonable use of her property. In any event, the ordinance is reasonable, constitutional and valid.

3. The trial court, in the exercise of its discretion, properly allowed the jury to take all the exhibits with them to the jury room (Code Crim. Pro., § 425). Moreover, when defendant's counsel objected, he did not specify any particular exhibit or objection, and he did not specifically except to the ruling.

 

2174 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Nassau County


48 Misc. 2d 536; 265 N.Y.S.2d 260; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1423



October 21, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, the application of the defendant, through his counsel, is granted and this matter is transferred to the Family Court. He is directed to appear there on October 25, 1965, pursuant to order of even date signed herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for a transfer of his criminal prosecution for second degree assault to the family court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the second degree assault of his live in girlfriend. Defendant applied for a transfer of the matter to family court. The court granted the application. Where a criminal complaint charged one with an assault of a member of the same household, upon timely request by the person charged, the matter had to be transferred to the family court.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's application.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Family Court -- assault between members of same household -- information charges defendant with felonious assault on lady with whom he lives; this charges "an assault between * * * members of the same * * * household" and hence is transferred to Family Court (Family Ct. Act, § 812).

An information in the District Court of Nassau County, charging defendant with felonious assault in the second degree (Penal Law, § 242, subd. 3) on a lady with whom he has been living as man and wife is, upon timely demand made by his counsel, the Public Defender of the county, ordered transferred to the Family Court in Nassau County. This is "an assault between * * * members of the same * * * household" (Family Ct. Act, § 812). Of course the court may then hold the defendant or admit him to bail or parole him (Family Ct. Act, §§ 813, 814, 815).

 

2175 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sacks v. Sacks


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


47 Misc. 2d 1050; 263 N.Y.S.2d 891; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1461



October 4, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff first wife's action to declare the nullity of the marriage of defendants, husband and second wife, the second wife filed a motion to dismiss the complaint as against her on jurisdictional grounds.


OVERVIEW: The husband, who was a resident of New York, obtained a Mexican divorce from the first wife, married the second wife, who was a resident of New York, in Connecticut, and took up residence in New Jersey. The first wife, also a resident of New York, filed an action to annul the husband's second marriage. Process was served upon the husband while he was working in New York City. Process was served upon the second wife while she was present in New Jersey. The second wife filed a motion to dismiss the complaint as against her, contending that court did not have jurisdiction over her. The court agreed. The court pointed out that where a defendant was a non-domiciliary of New York, service for in rem jurisdiction was permissible only if the res was within New York when jurisdiction was assumed. The res of the husband's second marriage was the husband and his second wife's matrimonial status, which was considered to have been transported to New Jersey when they moved there. Because the second wife was given only constructive service, the court did not have jurisdiction over her.


OUTCOME: The court granted the second wife's motion to dismiss the complaint as against her.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Husband and wife -- foreign divorce -- in action by first wife to declare nullity of husband's Mexican divorce and nullity of his marriage to second wife, as to latter action summons and complaint cannot constitutionally be served personally out of State on second wife, since she resides out of State and since her marital res is out of State (cf. Domestic Relations Law, § 140; § 230, subd. 3; CPLR 105, subd. [m]; 314, subd. 1).

1. Husband and wife were married in New York. Subsequently be obtained a Mexican divorce, and married another woman in Connecticut, and established his residence with her in New Jersey, but he maintains a place of business in New York. The first wife still lives in New York. She properly had him served in New York in this action to declare (1) the nullity of his Mexican divorce and (2) the nullity of his remarriage. Furthermore, as to cause (1), which involves the first marriage only, the summons and complaint may properly be served on his new wife outside of New York ( CPLR 314, subd. 1). But, as to cause (2), which involves the second marriage, the courts of New York cannot constitutionally obtain jurisdiction of the second wife by such out-of-State [***2] service, and the latter's motion for dismissal is therefore granted.

2. The Domestic Relations Law ( § 140; § 230, subd. 3), read with the CPLR (105, subd. [m]; 314, subd. 1), authorizes constructive service -- such as personal service out of State -- in an in rem matrimonial action between husband and wife; but these statutes cannot constitutionally be applied against a nonresident second wife in an action by a first wife to declare such second marriage void. Under the full faith and credit clause of the United States Constitution, the res of the second marriage is not in New York where the former wife resides, but is in New Jersey where the present wife and her husband reside now. The former wife cannot assert an in rem jurisdiction over such second wife's marriage.

 

2176 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miletich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Erie County


47 Misc. 2d 637; 262 N.Y.S.2d 993; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1516



September 10, 1965 



DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was acquitted of charges that he violated Buffalo City, N.Y. Ordinances § 381, the Home Improvement licensing ordinance. The City Court of Buffalo (New York) then granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that § 381 was so broad and vague as to be unconstitutional. The People appealed from the judgment granting the motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with painting premises without having obtained a license as required by the city's Home Improvement licensing ordinance, found at Buffalo City, N.Y. Ordinances § 381. Prior to the trial, defendant moved to dismiss the complaint. The city court reserved decision on the motion and directed the trial to commence. At the close of evidence, defendant renewed his motion to dismiss. The city court again reserved decision, and a judgment of acquittal was entered after a full trial. The city court thereafter granted the motion, holding that § 381 was so broad and vague as to be unconstitutional. The People appealed from the order of dismissal. The court dismissed the People's appeal. The court held that defendant's acquittal after a full trial did not give the People a right to appeal. The court held that were it to reversed the city court and order a new trial, defendant could claim that he was subjected to double jeopardy; thus, the court was unable to review the order. The court also stated that, in its opinion, the city court erred by directing the trial to proceed before rendering a decision on the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the People's appeal.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right of People to appeal -- People have no right to appeal from judgment of acquittal even though lower court held ordinance, with violation of which defendant was charged, unconstitutional.

Defendant was charged with a violation of the "Home Improvement" licensing ordinance of the City of Buffalo for failure to obtain a license before painting certain premises and, after trial, he was acquitted, the court holding the ordinance unconstitutional. This appeal must be dismissed because the People have no right to appeal from a judgment of acquittal. If the court on appeal held the ordinance constitutional, it could not order a new trial because defendant could claim that he was subject to double jeopardy.

 

2177 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Janks v. Syracuse


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Onondaga County


47 Misc. 2d 718; 263 N.Y.S.2d 227; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1535



September 2, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owner sought review of the order from the Superintendent of Building and Rehabilitation (New York), which required the demolition of the owner's building. The proceedings were commenced by an order obtained by the owner, which directed respondent city to show cause why a preliminary injunction should not be granted enjoining the city, until the determination of this action, from destroying the building.


OVERVIEW: The owner had a building that was sited for multiple violations of the city housing code. After the owner failed to correct the violations, the superintendent issued a final order to demolish the building. The petitioner did not demolish the building so the superintendent received bids for the demolition of the building. The owner obtained an order restraining the city from demolishing the building pending the hearing and determination of the appeal of the order. At the hearing, the court set aside and annulled the decision of the superintendent and remanded the case. The court concluded that: (1) the action by the superintendent was judicial or quasi-judicial because it involved the taking of or interference with the owner's property right; (2) a formal adversary hearing should have been held; (3) the housing code mandated that the superintendent provide notice to the owner, but such notice was never received; and (4) the owner was deprived of due process of law when the superintendent attempted to take his building without notice and an opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The court annulled and remanded the order of the superintendent and ordered the superintendent to proceed in accordance with the housing code in an attempt to correct violations at the building or take other appropriate action against the owner.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- dilapidated buildings -- court considers application as one under CPLR (art. 78) to review order of Superintendent of Building directing demolition of petitioner's building -- constitutionality of Housing Code cannot be determined in such proceeding -- order to demolish made without hearing on notice to petitioner as required by Housing Code constituted illegal exercise of authority and is annulled -- trial of petitioner held on three charges of violating Housing Code in Criminal Court did not warrant order or obviate requirement of hearing.

1. An application is considered as one made pursuant to CPLR 7801 to review an order issued by the Superintendent of Building of respondent city directing the demolition of petitioner's building since the court has jurisdiction of the necessary parties and CPLR 103 (subd. [c]) guarantees that no "civil judicial proceeding" shall be dismissed solely because it is cast in the wrong form.

2. A determination that the Housing Code of the City of Syracuse is unconstitutional cannot be made in a proceeding under CPLR (art. 78) because CPLR 7803 specifies what questions can be raised and the determination of constitutionality [***2] of an ordinance is not one of them.

3. Respondent determined that petitioner's building violated the Housing Code. Since the resulting order involved the taking of or interefence with a property right of petitioner, an adversary type hearing should have preceded the action and only facts supported by substantial evidence introduced at that hearing should be relied on in sustaining the action since the Housing Code itself provides for a hearing on notice preceding any action which the Superintendent of Building might take. Never was petitioner granted a hearing on any of the numerous violations of the Housing Code alleged to exist by the Superintendent. Because he failed to comply with the requirements of the Housing Code, his order and determination to demolish the building violated the code and constituted an illegal exercise of authority. His determination is annulled.

4. Petitioner was found guilty after trial in the city's Criminal Court of three violations of the code. The existence of these three violations did not warrant the determination to demolish nor does the trial obviate the requirement of the code that a hearing on notice, specifying the alleged defects, be held [***3] before the Superintendent of Building.

 

2178 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baird


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Nassau County


47 Misc. 2d 478; 262 N.Y.S.2d 947; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1544



August 31, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a demurrer to an information drawn against him for violation of the provisions of N.Y. Penal Law § 1142, which made it a misdemeanor to sell, lend, give, exhibit, or offer to sell, lend, give, etc. of any instrument or article or medicine for the prevention of conception.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled that defendant could not rely upon the decision of the United States Supreme Court which struck down a series of Connecticut statutes as unconstitutional as invading the privacy of the marital relationship. Defendant was not entitled to relief because he was, in effect, asking the court to enact new law rather than to interpret the laws on the books. Defendant was basing his contentions upon the social aspects of the law in question, rather than the legal aspects. The law relative to the sale, distribution, advertising, etc. of contraceptives, delineated in N.Y. Penal Law § 1142, had been held to be constitutional since 1917. When defendant was arrested and charged pursuant to § 1142, the law was as it was set forth, and defendant could not change that fact.


OUTCOME: The court disallowed defendant's demurrer.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- contraceptives -- statute forbidding sale of contraceptives is constitutional.

Despite changes developed by the modern trend, section 1142 of the Penal Law, which makes it a misdemeanor to sell any contraceptive, is constitutional and, if there is to be any change in such law, it must be enacted by the Legislature. Defendant's demurrer to the information is disallowed.

 

2179 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Orans v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


47 Misc. 2d 493; 262 N.Y.S.2d 893; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1564



August 24, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movants, a state assembly speaker and state senate president pro tempore, filed a motion for leave to intervene as petitioners in an action that concerned reapportionment of the state assembly and state senate. The speaker and president pro tempore also moved for an order for appointment of three referees for the purpose of the formulation of a comprehensive reapportionment plan of the assembly and senate.


OVERVIEW: The court had previously determined that a reapportionment plan for the assembly and senate approved by a three-judge federal district court violated provisions of the state constitution. Notwithstanding the affirmance of the court's prior determination by a state appellate court, a majority of the federal district court panel directed that special legislative elections be conducted under that plan even after a state appellate court had enjoined its use in the special elections. The court granted the motions for leave to intervene. The court deferred the motion for reference because it desired that the legislature was to have one last opportunity for enactment of a valid legislative reapportionment. The court held that it had to assume a supervisory role in the reapportionment process, ordered the imposition of deadlines upon the legislature, and was prepared for assurance that the next regular legislative election and a subsequent constitutional convention was to be had pursuant to a redistricting and reapportionment plan in conformity with the state constitution and the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court permitted the substitution of the speaker as a defendant and intervention of the president pro tempore as a plaintiff. The court established a deadline for respondents' submission of a reapportionment plan for the court's approval. If no plan were submitted, the court would formulate a plan for use in the next election, subject to the approval of a federal district court. The court deferred the motion for the appointment of referees.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Legislature -- Speaker of State Assembly permitted to intervene as respondent in proceeding to review legislative reapportionment plan approved by Federal court -- President pro tem of Senate entitled to intervene as petitioner -- proceeding not exhausted by prior final judgment affirmed by Court of Appeals -- appointment of Referees to formulate plan not subject to denial on basis of Glinski v. Lomenzo (16 N Y 2d 27) -- power to appoint Referees granted by CPLR 4001 -- Legislature is given opportunity to perform its primary responsibility of formulating constitutionally valid reapportionment plan, but subject to supervision of court as stated.

1. Since the Speaker of the New York State Assembly was a necessary party in the original proceeding to review a legislative reapportionment, his right to intervene in this proceeding to review a legislative reapportionment approved by the Federal court is absolute, but as a party respondent, to be substituted for another.

2. The President pro tem of the State Senate is entitled to intervene as a party petitioner either under CPLR 1012 (subd. [a], par. 2) or CPLR 1013. The interests of all the [***2] citizens are inadequately represented by present petitioners who oppose a request for affirmative relief at this time when such a request is in the best interest of the citizenry.

3. Even though this proceeding resulted in a final judgment (45 Misc 2d 616) affirmed by the Court of Appeals (15 N Y 2d 339), the proceeding is not exhausted. In order to give effect to that prior judgment, the court must fashion some immediate and continuing relief, and the instant applications are appropriate for that purpose.

4. Relief by way of appointment of Referees to formulate a constitutional reapportionment plan need not be denied on the basis of Glinski v. Lomenzo (16 N Y 2d 27).

5. A reference under article 43 of the CPLR is inapposite. CPLR 4001 empowers the court to appoint Referees in the ordinary course of events.

6. Since the primary responsibility for apportionment rests with the Legislature, the Legislature is given another opportunity to enact a constitutionally valid reapportionment plan before the court will formulate its own plan of reapportionment. The court defers decision on the employment of a panel of Referees. However, it assumes a supervisory role in reapportionment.  [***3] Accordingly, respondents are directed to submit a plan to reapportion the Senate and Assembly which complies with the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and with all applicable provisions of the New York State Constitution not in conflict with the United States Constitution on or before February 1, 1966. Upon their failure to do so, the court shall undertake formulation of a reapportionment plan which shall, with Federal District Court approval, govern the November, 1966 election of members of the Legislature, and the court may at any time appoint Referees to assist in the formulation of a plan if it determines that respondents are not proceeding with diligence to complete a plan before February 1, 1966.

 

2180 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Onondaga County


50 Misc. 2d 357; 270 N.Y.S.2d 434; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1586



August 12, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the foregoing reasons, the judgment of conviction is affirmed in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Syracuse City Court (New York), which convicted him of a violation of N. Y. Penal Law § 722(2) and of a violation of City of Syracuse, N. Y. Rev. Gen. Ordinance § 38-a, ch. 16, art. 11. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his demurrer to the information charging a violation of the city ordinance on the ground that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to the police station, seeking response to his letter to the police chief. The chief was not in, and he was asked to make an appointment for a later time. Evidence was controverted as to whether defendant then stood at one side of the stairway or whether he walked back and forth on the stairs, blocking access. Defendant was charged with violating City of Syracuse Rev. Gen. Ordinance § 38, ch. 16, art. 11, which prohibited loitering about a public building so as to prevent access by others. Defendant demurred to the charge, arguing that the ordinance was void for vagueness. The city court convicted him and he sought review. The court affirmed. The court found that an anti-loitering provision would be void if it did not distinguish between conduct that was innocent and conduct that was harmful. The court noted that the Syracuse ordinance prohibited loitering that was coupled with impeding access and the conduct of business. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional. The court rejected defendant's argument that the ordinance prevented lawful assembly, finding that a lawful demonstration was underway outside the building when defendant was arrested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violating the city's anti-loitering statute over his contention that the ordinance was void for vagueness.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- loitering -- city ordinance prohibiting loitering in public building is constitutional where it prohibits specific stated conduct -- ordinance does not prohibit right to petition or to demonstrate publicly -- evidence established defendant's guilt of violating ordinance beyond reasonable doubt -- defendant's conduct on stairway and refusal to obey reasonable police order violated Penal Law ( § 722, subd. 2) -- defendant's conviction did not violate his constitutional rights of assembly, free speech and petition.

1. A city ordinance providing that no person shall loiter in a public building or obstruct stairways so as to prevent free access by members of the public or interfere with or interrupt the conduct of business in offices of such building is not unconstitutional. Loitering is coupled with specific prohibited conduct.

2. The ordinance does not prohibit the right to petition or to publicly demonstrate. Picketing was being conducted in a peaceable manner without interference by the police in the immediate vicinity of the public building here. The standards under the present [***2] city ordinance established definite guide lines for the police. The presumption of validity of the ordinance has not been overcome nor has the presumption of its inherent constitutionality been overcome.

3. The evidence established that defendant violated the ordinance beyond a reasonable doubt.

4. It also showed that defendant's conduct upon the stairway of the public building and refusal to obey the reasonable police order was such as to violate subdivision 2 of section 722 of the Penal Law.

5. Defendant's conviction did not violate his constitutional rights of assembly, free speech and petition. The rights of the entire group to picket were not interfered with.

 

2181 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Himmel v. Chase Manhattan Bank


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Trial Term, New York County


47 Misc. 2d 93; 262 N.Y.S.2d 515; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1598



August 9, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, respondents' motion to dismiss this article 7-A proceeding, on the ground that this legislative enactment is unconstitutional, be and the same hereby is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mortgagee filed a motion to dismiss petitioner tenants' proceeding under art. 7-A of the N.Y. Real Prop. Acts Law to deposit rent into court. The mortgagee claimed that art. 7-A, retroactively applied, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Art. 7-A was enacted after this dispute arose between the tenants and the mortgagee, which had bought in the property in foreclosure. The tenants claimed that the failure of the central air conditioning system and other conditions in the building were health hazards, and desired to pay their rent into court and have it directed to fixing the conditions. In denying the mortgagee's motion to dismiss the petition, the court held that art. 7-A was a remedial statute, and retroactive application of remedial statutes was generally constitutional. The court held that art. 7-A merely enlarged an existing remedy in N.Y. Real Prop. Acts. Law § 755. The court held that art. 7-A was a valid and not unreasonable exercise of the police power, and noted that so long as a law was reasonable, a court could not inquire into the wisdom of its enactment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the mortgagee's motion to dismiss the tenant's petition to deposit rent into court.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- multiple dwellings -- one third of tenants of multiple dwelling, even if it is high class and beyond rent control, and even if no departmental violations have been filed, may petition New York City Civil Court for leave to deposit rents in court and for court to appoint administrator to use such rents towards remedying conditions which are dangerous to life, health or safety of occupants (Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, art. 7-A) -- statute applies to rents which were already past-due when statute took effect on July 17, 1965.

Chapter 909 of the Laws of 1965 (adding art. 7-A to Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, and amending New York City Civil Court Act) declares the legislative intent to police judicially conditions which are dangerous to the life, health or safety of the occupants of multiple dwellings, regardless of the building's age or location, and authorizes a proceeding to be instituted by one third of the tenants in such a multiple [***2] dwelling in the City of New York for a judgment permitting the tenants to deposit the rents in court and directing that a court-appointed administrator apply such rents towards remedying such conditions. The statute is a valid and constitutional exercise of the police power, and the New York City Civil Court so determines ( CPLR 603). The remedy provided by this statute is in addition to other remedies (cf. Real Property Actions and Proceedings Law, art. 7, § 755; Multiple Dwelling Law, § 309). The court may entertain the petition even though no departmental violations have been filed against the building. Furthermore, the statute applies to rents which were already past-due on the statute's effective date, July 17, 1965. This remedial statute may be particularly appropriately applied to a high-class multiple dwelling such as this one, which is not rent-controlled, and where, therefore, the City Rent and Rehabilitation Administrator cannot reduce the rents to $ 1 and thus persuade the landlord to make the necessary repairs or replacements. The question remains to be tried whether the conditions in this building are indeed dangerous to life, health or safety of occupants.

 

2182 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Collins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Orange County


47 Misc. 2d 210; 261 N.Y.S.2d 970; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1603



August 5, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The sentence is hereby modified to strike out therefrom the provision imposing an additional period of commitment to the County Jail in the event of the nonpayment of the fine.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the sentence of 11 months and 29 days imposed on him by the Court of Special Sessions of the Village of Goshen (New York) pursuant to his conviction for assault in the third degree on the basis that the imposition of an extra day's confinement for each $ 1 of a $ 250 fine that was not paid was violative of his constitutional right to equal protection as he was unable to pay the fine due to indigency.


OVERVIEW: In rendering an opinion on defendant's appeal of his sentence, the court found that the imposition of fines was constitutional because N.Y. Penal Law § 484 specifically vested in sentencing judges the power to impose a fine and N.Y. Penal Law § 718 provided that a convicted person could be detained in jail until the fine was paid for a period of time not to exceed one day for each $ 1 of the fine unpaid. The court noted that such additional detention after a maximum sentence for a failure to pay the fine had been sanctioned, not as a continuation of the period of imprisonment pursuant to the sentence, but on the specific ground that it was an effective means to enable the court to enforce the collection of the obligatory and properly imposed fine. However, when applied to indigent persons, § 718 had the effect of a denial of equal protection because the inability to pay the fine resulted in indigents spending extended periods incarcerated merely because of a lack of funds, in opposition to the state law that required nondiscriminatory treatment of all defendants without regard to their financial worth. Thus, the court modified defendant's sentence by eliminating the fine penalty.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's sentence and struck the provision that imposed an additional period of commitment to the county jail for the nonpayment of the fine.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sentence -- as applied to indigent defendant, statute which permits court to impose additional day in jail for each dollar of fine unpaid contravenes constitutional right to equal protection of laws (Code Crim. Pro., §§ 484, 718; U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.); such additional portion of sentence is stricken.

1. The statutory provision that a judgment of conviction and imprisonment and fine may further direct that the defendant be imprisoned for one day for every dollar of the fine unpaid (L. 1876, ch. 61; Code Crim. Pro., §§ 484, 718) is unconstitutional as applied to an indigent defendant who cannot pay the fine (U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.).

2. Defendant was convicted, by a Justice of the Peace, of third degree assault and was sentenced to 11 months and 29 days in the County Jail and a fine of $ 250, and, additionally, in default of payment of the fine, to an additional day in jail for each dollar of the fine unpaid. This additional provision is now stricken by the County Court, since defendant's [***2] indigency is not disputed.

 

2183 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


R. B. I. Enterprises, Inc. v. Rochester


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial and Special Term, Monroe County


47 Misc. 2d 527; 262 N.Y.S.2d 939; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1639



July 27, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed a declaratory judgment action (New York), requesting the court to direct defendant city to issue a permit for construction within a proposed mapped street bed. The landowners requested that the court declare that the city's refusal to permit the landowners to build on a proposed street bed constituted an appropriation of the landowners' property without just compensation or due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The landowners alleged that the city's refusal to permit them to build on a proposed street bed constituted an appropriation of their property without just compensation or due process of law and was unconstitutional. The court found that the effect of the official city map lessened the value and limited the free and independent use of the landowners' property. The court additionally found that the proposed widening of the street at issue would be of little, if any, direct benefit to the landowners. The court concluded that if the landowners were required to set their building back, then for all practical purposes there would be a taking of a 14-foot strip. Once the building was erected, that 14-foot area, upon which the landowners were obliged to pay taxes, would be of no apparent practical or economic value. That factor alone would substantially damage the landowners. The court concluded that the landowners were entitled to relief. The court held that N.Y. Gen. City Law § 35 and the official map of the city were unconstitutional and void to the extent that their application prevented the landowners from constructing the building within the area of the proposed street widening.


OUTCOME: The court held that the landowners were entitled to judgment, with costs, declaring that the state statute at issue and the official map of the city were void to the extent that their application prevented the landowners from constructing the building. The court ordered that the city issue necessary building permits to the landowners upon presentation of plans for the building.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- street plans -- owners of land, portion of which lies in bed of proposed street widening, are entitled to building permit or to have city buy bed of street; General City Law ( § 35) denying permit to land in bed of proposed street, and street plan are unconstitutional.

Plaintiffs, owners of property on the south side of a street, 30 feet of which a 1930 street plan indicated would be required to widen the street (reduced to 14 feet by a 1963 amendment) having presented plans for construction of a building on their property including the 14-foot portion, which their business requires, are entitled to a building permit, or if the municipality refuses a permit, it must buy the 14-foot strip. Section 35 of the General City Law which forbids the issuance of a permit for construction in the bed of a street laid out on a plan, the official map of defendant city and the ordinances establishing it take plaintiffs' property for public use without just compensation and are unconstitutional and void.

 

2184 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Sullivan County Democratic Committee


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Sullivan County


47 Misc. 2d 60; 261 N.Y.S.2d 697; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1643



July 26, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion for temporary injunction is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff committeeman filed a motion for a temporary injunction in his action against defendants, committee and chairman, for a declaratory judgment to have N.Y. Elec. Law § 12 declared unconstitutional as it related to the method in which county committees of political parties could be constituted. He also sought to have a section of the committee rules that established the method in designating members declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the committeeman's argument depended upon the application of the one person, one vote principle of law to the method of electing committeemen to comprise the committee. The principle required that seats in state legislatures be apportioned on a population basis and that political equality required that each person received one vote. The one person, one vote rule was also applicable to the apportionment of elected members of legislative bodies of governmental units below the level of state legislatures. The court held that entities such as the committee in question was not an entity to which the one person, one vote rule had been applied. A political committee could not be considered a legislative body of a governmental unit. The court held that the one person, one vote principle was not intended to be applicable to quasi public organizations and thus, the committeeman had no grounds to attack the constitutionality of N.Y. Elec. Law § 12. Additionally, because the committee was an unincorporated voluntary association in which no rights of property or personal liberty were involved, the court had no equitable jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the committeeman's motion.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- county committee of party -- temporary injunction denied in action to declare that unequal representation of enrolled voters by county committeemen of political party (Election Law, § 12) is unconstitutional.

The principle, "one person, one vote" ( Reynolds v. Sims, 377 U.S. 533), does not require that the members of the county committee of a political party shall each represent the same number of enrolled voters of the party; in any event, the Sullivan County Democratic Committee member who seeks a judgment declaring the unconstitutionality of section 12 of the Election Law, which provides for election of county committeemen by election districts and which fails to provide for the fact that some election districts have far more enrolled party members than do other election districts (but, see Election Law, § 64, subds. 1, 6), has failed to show a clear right to an injunction pending the trial of this action; hence no such injunction will issue.

 

2185 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Arglo Painting Corp. v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


47 Misc. 2d 618; 263 N.Y.S.2d 124; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1647



July 26, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application is denied, and the stay is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding before the court, petitioner, a corporation that was a bidder of work involving repairing, painting, and refinishing (corporation), sought an order to direct respondent, a municipal board of education, to qualify the corporation as eligible for the award of a certain contract and to direct the board of education to execute the contract with the corporation as the low bidder.


OVERVIEW: The board of education had been notified, after investigations into bid rigging on public contracts, that a painting and decorating contractor had refused to sign a waiver of immunity. Such refusal, pursuant to law, automatically disqualified the contractor and any firm of which he was a member or officer from thereafter submitting bids to or receiving awards from any municipal corporation. Subsequently, the corporation submitted the lowest bid for alterations and repairs on a certain high school. It was discovered that the corporation "fronted" for the disqualified contractor. Consequently, the board of education advised the corporation that its request for qualification as a bidder was disapproved and that it was not the lowest responsible bidder for the contract. The court affirmed. The court found that (1) the fact that the corporation submitted the lowest bid did not, as a matter of law, establish it as the lowest responsible bidder; and (2) the board of education, as an awarding agency, had the duty of determining whether the corporation possessed integrity and moral worth or was, in fact, a front for the disqualified contractor.


OUTCOME: The court denied the corporation's application to be qualified as eligible for the award of the contract and vacated the stay. The court found that the corporation was not the lowest responsible bidder for the contract.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- bids and bidders -- application for order directing Board of Education to qualify corporation as eligible low bidder for award of contract involving repair of school denied -- board found that individual who had been disqualified from bidding was real party in interest in affairs of corporation and latter was not lowest "responsible" bidder -- corporation had no property interest in contract by reason of submitting lowest bid, had no right to hearing and cannot attack constitutionality of statute relative to disqualification -- court may not interfere with lawful exercise of discretion by board.

1. An application for an order directing the Board of Education of the City of New York to qualify petitioner, a corporation, as the eligible low bidder for the award of a contract involving repair of a school is denied. Although petitioner's bid was the lowest submitted, an investigation by the board resulted in findings that a certain individual who had, because of refusal to waive immunity during an investigation as to bid rigging been disqualified, pursuant to section 103-b of the General Municipal Law, from bidding [***2] on board work, was the real party in interest in petitioner's affairs, that petitioner acted for said individual in submitting the bid in question, and that petitioner was not the lowest "responsible" bidder (Education Law, § 2556, subd. 10; General Municipal Law, § 103, subd. 1) and, in the public interest, should not be given the award. Petitioner did not obtain a property interest in the contract merely because it submitted the lowest bid and, accordingly, did not have the right to a hearing before being disqualified.

2. Since petitioner was not deprived of a property right, it cannot attack, as violative of due process, the provision of section 103-a of the General Municipal Law relative to automatic disqualification of a bidder who refuses to waive immunity.

3. The board's duty to determine the qualification of a bidder was a judicial function which was exhausted when it made a proper investigation and findings reasonably based thereon. The court may not interfere with its lawful exercise of discretion.

 

2186 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rapaport v. Messina


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


47 Misc. 2d 394; 262 N.Y.S.2d 815; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1663



July 20, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, operators of a bar and grill located in a village, initiated proceedings against respondents, the village board of trustees, its mayor, and a building inspector, under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to prohibit respondents from proceeding against petitioners under the State Standard Building Code For Places of Public Assembly (Building Code) and to review the action of respondents denying petitioners a permit for a curb lowering.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were also owners of the real property containing the licensed premises. Petitioners alleged that the building inspector appeared at petitioners' bar and placed a hand-written sign upon an interior wall of the premises containing the following legend: "Occupancy by more than 30 persons in bar, 32 persons in dining room was dangerous and unlawful." Respondents justified the action by citing N.Y. Labor Law § 110 and §§ 36-2.2(b)(10), (11) of the State Standard Building Code for Places of Public Assembly, N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 12, § 36-2.2. The court held, however, that petitioners' premises did not come within any of the three categories enumerated in the N.Y. Labor Law § 2(12). Petitioners further alleged discriminatory enforcement. The court noted that there were some 60 licensed bars in the village. Significantly, only petitioners' establishment had been so placarded and restricted. In the absence of any denial, the court was required to assume that to be so. As to respondents' refusal to issue a permit for a curb cut, the court held that respondents' action exhibited a pattern which could only be characterized as arbitrary, unreasonable, and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of petitioners.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- limitation upon occupancy of bar and grill -- permit to lower curb -- Village of Port Chester may not invoke State Standard Building Code for Places of Public Assembly to justify imposition of limitation upon occupancy of bar and grill -- if there is danger of overcrowding, municipality should enforce local building code or enact appropriate legislation -- pattern of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement is indicated -- rejection of application for permit to lower curb constituted deprivation of substantial property right without due process -- where use is lawful, act of granting permission to lower curbs is purely ministerial -- local authorities have available recourses if bar patrons engage in noisome offenses.

1. A bar and grill operated by petitioners in the Village of Port Chester is not a "place of public assembly" as defined in section 2 (subd. 12) of the Labor Law. Accordingly, section 36-2.2 (subd. [b], pars. [10], [11]) of the State Standard Building Code for Places of Public Assembly (12 NYCRR 36-2.2), applicable to such places, may not be cited by respondents, the said village and various officials thereof, to justify their [***2] imposition of a limitation upon the occupancy of the said premises.

2. If there is a danger of overcrowding, the municipality should enforce the applicable local building code or enact appropriate legislation. Furthermore, petitioners have operated the premises for four years and have been licensed by the State Liquor Authority, an agency known for its regulation of the physical characteristics of establishments under its jurisdiction.

3. Of some 60 licensed bars in the village, only that of petitioners has been restricted in occupancy. This indicates a pattern of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement which cannot be condoned.

4. Also arbitrary and discriminatory is respondents' rejection of petitioners' application for removal of a parking meter in front of their property and for a permit to lower a curb in order to create an off-street parking area. This rejection, unaccompanied by any affirmative findings and apparently based only upon a petition of aggrieved neighbors, deprived petitioners of a substantial property right without due process.

5. Where the use is lawful, the act of granting permission to lower curbs is purely ministerial.

6. If the patrons of petitioners'  [***3] bar publicly engage in noisome offenses, the local authorities have available recourses.

 

2187 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Augostini v. Lasky


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Broome County


46 Misc. 2d 1058; 262 N.Y.S.2d 594; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1667



July 20, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the citizens, taxpayers, and qualified voters of Broome County, filed a motion for summary judgment in their action against defendant members of the Broome County Board of Supervisors (New York). Plaintiffs requested that the court declare unconstitutional and illegal the representation and voting procedure of the Board, and other relief.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that there was a gross disparity in population among the municipalities represented on the Board. Plaintiffs argued that the disparity resulted in an arbitrary impairment of the votes of plaintiffs and of all those similarly situated by means of an invidiously discriminatory geographic classification. Plaintiffs asserted that the discrimination deprived plaintiffs of liberty and property without due process of law and of the equal protection of the laws in violation of federal and state constitutions. The court held that the "one person, one vote" principle applied to the election of members of the Board, and the present apportionment with respect to the town supervisors and the districting of the city wards violated the equal protection provision of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and N.Y. Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 11. The court rejected defendants' affirmative defense that the people had voted for such apportionment. The court held that an individual's constitutionally protected right to cast an equally weighted vote could not be denied even by a vote of a majority.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the districting and apportionment of members of the Board violated state and federal Constitutions' equal protection provisions, but the Board would continue to function as constituted. Unless a constitutionally acceptable method of districting became effective prior thereto, the supervisors to be chosen at the next election were to be chosen under existing law. The court retained jurisdiction to review districting plans.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Board of Supervisors of county -- Supreme Court has jurisdiction of action for judgment declaring that present representation on Board of Supervisors of Broome County is unconstitutional -- method of apportionment of wards and towns whereby voters representing 20% of population elect majority of board is unconstitutional -- section 150 of County Law and section 11 of Second Class Cities Law insofar as they require present districting of county are unconstitutional -- defense that voters at election rejected broadening of voting power for Supervisors of more populous wards and towns is insufficient -- relief to plaintiffs is stated.

1. The Supreme Court has jurisdiction to entertain an action for judgment declaring unconstitutional the present representation and voting procedure of the Board of Supervisors of Broome County.

2.
