A method of apportionment of the wards and towns of Broome County whereby the 15 least populous wards and towns, representing less than 20% of the population of the county, elect a majority of the Board of Supervisors violates the "one person, one vote" principle and the equal protection provision of the Fourteenth [***2] Amendment of the United States Constitution and sections 1 and 11 of article I of the State Constitution.

3. Section 150 of the County Law and section 11 of the Second Class Cities Law, insofar as the application of each of the sections requires the present districting or apportionment of the Broome County Board of Supervisors violates the said constitutional provisions.

4. A defense that in an election held in 1963 and in 1964 the People rejected propositions to give the Supervisors of the more populous wards and towns greater voting power is insufficient.

5. The relief granted to plaintiffs is stated.

People v. Kahl


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Nassau County


46 Misc. 2d 1088; 262 N.Y.S.2d 23; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1668



July 19, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In view of the foregoing this court finds the defendant not guilty upon each of the counts contained in the information charging him with violations of sections 2143 and 2147 of the Penal Law and said information is accordingly in all respects dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violations of N.Y. Penal Law § 2143, which prohibited the performance of labor on Sunday, and N.Y. Penal Law § 2147, which barred the public selling or offering for sale of goods on Sunday.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a sales employee of a New York corporation engaged in the business of constructing, selling, and installing swimming pools. The corporation maintained a showroom, wherein it exhibited for display three swimming pools of varying design, each of which was permanently affixed to the realty and hence not of themselves for sale. On Sundays the showroom was visited on an average by between 8 to 25 persons during the hours of noon to 5:00 p.m. in groups of approximately, two, four, six, or eight. Most of the contracts of sale were consummated at the customers' homes after their premises had been examined and their requirements precisely ascertained. At the time of defendant's arrest there were only two prospective customers on the premises who had come that day merely to "browse around." The court found no violation of the Fourteenth Amendment by the selective prosecution of defendant because there was no pattern of discrimination consciously practiced. However, the court found that the evidence failed to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that an offer to sell was actually made by defendant, that prices were quoted, money accepted, or a memorandum of sale executed.


OUTCOME: The court found defendant not guilty upon each of the counts contained in the information charging him with violations of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 2143, 2147 and, accordingly, dismissed the information.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Sabbath laws -- showroom for sale of swimming pools to be installed in realty was open on Sundays, but People did not prove that any offers of sales were made to two prospective customers; salesman is not guilty of breaking Sabbath laws -- no evidence that defendant or his employer has been singled out for prosecution in violation of constitutional right to equal protection of laws.

1. A swimming pool corporation maintains a showroom or show place where it exhibits three swimming pools, each of different design, and each permanently installed in and affixed to the realty. The showroom is open on Sundays and is visited on that day by between 8 and 25 persons. They come there to "browse around". Most sales, if any, are consummated subsequently at people's homes. On the Sunday when defendant, a sales employee, was arrested, the only potential customers in the place were a man and wife. The evidence does not [***2] establish beyond a reasonable doubt that any offer to sell was actually made. Defendant is found not guilty of violating the Sabbath laws (Penal Law, §§ 2143, 2147; see, also, § 2140) and the information is dismissed.

2. There is no evidence that this defendant or his corporate employer was singled out for prosecution in violation of his right to the equal protection of the laws (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 11; U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.).

 

2189 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Derman v. Ingraham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Ulster County


47 Misc. 2d 346; 262 N.Y.S.2d 533; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1717



June 30, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In my opinion, therefore, the plaintiffs are neither being arbitrarily discriminated against by the proposed licensure nor do they come within the exemptions to the statute. There being no substantial questions of fact requiring a trial, the motion for a temporary injunction is denied, and judgment may be entered on the pleadings in favor of the defendant, without costs. A stay of 10 days after entry and service of the judgment herein is also granted herewith in order to allow the plaintiffs, if so advised, to seek a review by an appellate court and apply for a stay pending such review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, licensed pathologists and a pathology association, sought a judgment declaring certain provisions of 1964 N.Y. Laws ch. 217 unconstitutional and invalid as to them, and others similarly situated, because, they alleged, it required dual licensing for medical doctors performing certain pathology services.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 572 and N.Y. Pub. Health Law art. 5, tit. V, § 579. The contention was that the statute required dual licensure of those licensed to practice medicine who engage in the specialty of pathology, while those who practice medicine in other fields needed only to possess a single license issued by the Department of Education. Plaintiffs sought a temporary injunction restraining defendant Commissioner of Health from enforcing against them the challenged provisions. The defendant cross-claimed for a dismissal of the complaint, or judgment on the pleadings. The court entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of the Commissioner. The court held that the state legislature passed the law to ensure safety in delivering healthcare to the public. The law was not arbitrary and was rationally related to a legitimate state interest of protecting the public from shoddy laboratory practices. The distinction between physicians who operated laboratories for use by others and those who had laboratories as adjuncts to their practices was a legitimate classification with a reasonable and rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment on the pleadings in favor of the Commissioner.


HEADNOTES

Health -- licensing of clinical laboratories -- Public Health Law (art. 5, tit. V) providing for licensing of clinical laboratories is within police power and constitutional -- distinction between physicians operating laboratories for benefit of other physicians and those who perform laboratory tests for their own patients is reasonable -- Legislature could require director of laboratory, already licensed as physician, to procure separate license as director -- exempting Federal and State laboratories from statute is also reasonable.

1. Title V of article 5 of the Public Health Law ( §§ [***2] 570-581) which provides for the licensing of clinical laboratories and establishes minimum qualifications for laboratory directors is reasonably related to the public health and welfare, is within the police power of the State, and is constitutional.

2. The distinction between physicians who operate laboratories for the diagnostic benefit of other physicians and those who perform laboratory tests solely as an adjunct to the treatment of their own patients is a classification which has a reasonable and rational basis and is within the power of the Legislature to make, and does not deny plaintiffs the equal protection of the laws.

3. The Legislature could reasonably conclude that the qualifications which one must possess to practice medicine, including the specialty of pathology, are different from those necessary to insure the proper direction of a clinical laboratory, and therefore could reasonably require the director of a laboratory to procure a separate certificate of qualification, even though licensed as a physician, to administer the laboratory.

4. Exempting Federal and State laboratories from the provisions of the statute may also be considered to be a reasonable classification [***3] since the Commissioner of Health has no jurisdiction over facilities operated by the Federal authorities and State laboratories are already controlled by the department having jurisdiction.

 

2190 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rappaport v. Gaynor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Bronx County


75 Misc. 2d 649; 348 N.Y.S.2d 451; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1205



June 28, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, as there is warrant in the record for the determination of the respondent, and a rational basis for his order, the applications of landlord and tenants are both denied and the petitions dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners were the landlord and tenants of a housing project constructed and operated pursuant to N.Y. Priv. Hous. Fin. Law art. 2. The tenants sought review and annulment a determination of respondent, Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal of the State of New York, which granted an increase in rents. The landlord sought review and modification of the order granting the increase because the increase was applied in two steps.


OVERVIEW: The landlord filed an application for an increase in rent on the ground that the income from the privately funded project was insufficient to meet its requirement. The Commissioner approved the rent increase and stated that it was to be made in two steps. The tenants appealed the decision because they challenged the rent increase. The landlord challenged the requirement that it be made in two steps. The court found that there was a rational basis for the Commissioner's decision and denied and dismissed the petitions of the tenants and landlord. N.Y. Priv. Hous. Fin. Law § 31(1)(a) contemplated that the rents might be varied and that there might be a deficiency in the payment to landlords which would be made up in a subsequent year, pursuant to N.Y. Priv. Hous. Fin. Law § 28. It was a proper exercise of the Commissioner's discretion to have the increase in two steps to lessen the impact on the tenants. The fact that the power to do so was not specifically provided for under the law did not bar his action. A tax abatement matter set forth by the landlord was considered and, if secured, relief would be afforded to the tenants.


OUTCOME: The court denied and dismissed the petitions of the tenants and the landlord.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- limited profit housing -- State Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal properly granted rent increase in two stages -- leases validly provided that Commissioner could authorize rent increases during term of leases.

The State Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal properly determined and ordered that the average maximum monthly rents in a limited profit housing project should be increased by $ 1.70 a room effective April 1, 1965 and by an additional $ 1.70 a room effective April 1, 1966, and that, if the landlord's pending application to increase its tax abatement from 40% to 50% were successful, he would entertain an application to modify this rent increase (Private Housing Finance Law, art. 2, §§ 28, 31). The leases validly provided that the rents could be raised during the term of a lease, with the approval of the Commissioner. His determination has a rational basis and is warranted by the facts. Judicial review petitions ( CPLR [***2] art. 78) by the landlord and by tenants are both dismissed.

 

2191 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Shilbury v. Board of Supervisors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Sullivan County


46 Misc. 2d 837; 260 N.Y.S.2d 931; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1734



June 26, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an elector, filed a motion for summary judgment in his declaratory judgment action against defendants, a county board of supervisors and the State of New York, seeking a declaration that N.Y. County Law art. 4 was unconstitutional and that it was the duty of the board to formulate a system under which the vote of each supervisor would be proportionate to the number of persons represented by him. The board filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The county consisted of 15 towns of varying populations. Each town had one supervisor with one vote on the board. The elector filed a complaint seeking reapportionment of the votes of the supervisors. The State was made a party defendant. The elector filed a motion for summary judgment and defendants filed a motion to dismiss. The court granted the elector's motion. The "one person, one vote" principle was applicable to the apportionment of elected members of boards of supervisors and other legislative bodies of governmental units below the level of State legislatures. The scheme of apportionment of the members of the board did not conform to the "one person, one vote" principle and was in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. XVI and N.Y. Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 11. The court had jurisdiction of the subject matter of the action. Although the elector enjoyed an advantage by the scheme because the population of his town was less than 1/15th of the total population of the county, there were seven towns with populations less than his town. Because the relevant facts in the case were matters of public record, there was no issue of fact precluding summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the elector. The court declared that the present apportionment of the board and the relevant provision of New York County Law as applied to the apportionment of the board violated equal protection. The court ordered that the supervisors be allowed to complete their statutory two-year terms, and that a system of weighted voting be implemented until a proper method of apportionment was devised.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Supervisors of county -- "one person, one vote" principle is applicable to apportionment of members of Boards of Supervisors -- scheme of apportionment of Sullivan County Board of Supervisors violates Federal and State Constitutions; section 150 of County Law as applicable to present apportionment of Board of Supervisors violates said constitutional provisions -- vote of plaintiff, as resident of town, is diluted -- court has jurisdiction of subject matter -- since no issues of fact exist, plaintiff is entitled to declaratory judgment -- weighted voting is ordered to redress wrong.

1. The "one person, one vote" principle is applicable to the apportionment of elected members of Boards of Supervisors and other legislative bodies of governmental units below the level of State Legislatures.

2. The scheme of apportionment of the Board of Supervisors of Sullivan County whereby the population of the towns vary from 356 to 8,792, and eight Supervisors, representing slightly less than 20% of the county's population, can prevail over seven representing slightly more than 80% of the population, does not conform to the "one person, one vote" principle [***2] and is in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and sections 1 and 11 of article I of the New York Constitution. Section 150 of the County Law, as applicable to the present apportionment of the Sullivan County Board of Supervisors, violates said constitutional provisions.

3. That plaintiff resides in a town which has a smaller population than others nevertheless disenfranchises him, since there are towns with smaller populations so that his vote is diluted and undervalued.

4. The court has jurisdiction of the subject matter of the action.

5. Since there are no issues of fact, plaintiff is entitled to declaratory judgment.

6. Weighted voting is ordered as a temporary measure to redress the wrong. It obviates a special election, permits Supervisors to serve the statutory two-year term and allows additional time in which to formulate an acceptable permanent plan of apportionment.

 

2192 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Marsh


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


46 Misc. 2d 777; 260 N.Y.S.2d 893; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1737



June 25, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to suppress is granted, the information (complaint) is dismissed and defendant is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence of contraband and a motion to dismiss the charge of illegal possession of contraband, which was in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1747-d.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on a charge of disorderly conduct. After his arrest, he was searched by police and contraband was found on him. He was then charged with illegal possession. After a trial on the first charge, defendant was acquitted. During the trial on the possession charge, defendant filed motions to suppress the evidence found by the officer after the arrest for disorderly conduct and to dismiss the possession charge. The court granted the motions. The court rejected the State's argument that "offenses" were included in "crimes" for the purposes of 1963 N.Y. Laws § 580, which amended N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 177. The court held that 1963 N.Y. Laws § 580 did not change the fact that an acquittal of a charge involved in an original arrest invalidated the search which revealed the unrelated basis of a second charge. The court found that the search after the arrest for disorderly conduct was improper because defendant was acquitted on that charge. Therefore, the contraband had to be suppressed as fruits of the poisonous tree.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion to suppress and motion to dismiss the information against him, and discharged him.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- contraband found on defendant in search following arrest for disorderly conduct is suppressed where defendant was acquitted of charge of disorderly conduct; acquittal invalidated search.

Contraband found on the person of defendant in a search following his arrest for disorderly conduct, an offense, must be suppressed where defendant was acquitted of the charge of disorderly conduct. The acquittal of the charge involved in the original arrest ipso facto invalidated the search which revealed the contraband, the basis of the second charge. Such result is required by People v. Dreares (15 A D 2d 204, affd. 11 N Y 2d 906) and subdivision 1 of section 177 of the Code of Criminal Procedure which enables an officer to arrest a person without a warrant for a crime committed or attempted in his presence, as amended in 1963 so as to provide "or where a police officer * * * has reasonable grounds for believing that a crime is being committed in his presence", has not changed the result. The offense of disorderly conduct is [***2] not a "crime" within the amendment even though procedurally it is treated as one.

Poughkeepsie v. Hopper Plumbing & Heating Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Dutchess County


46 Misc. 2d 761; 260 N.Y.S.2d 901; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1741



June 24, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The complaint is thus dismissed and the temporary injunction is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, plumbing contractor and school districts, challenged an order from the Appellate Division, Second Department (New York) that affirmed a trial court's grant of a preliminary injunction prohibiting the contractor from performing plumbing work in the construction of schools until it complied with the Poughkeepsie, N.Y., Plumbing Code and Ordinance (Code).


OVERVIEW: The school districts awarded contracts to the plumbing contractor for the construction of new schools. Although the contractor submitted no plans for the contracts and made no application for a certificate of competency with plaintiff city, it obtained all of the required approvals from the state and began work on the schools. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction to the city, and the intermediate appellate court affirmed that order. But on appeal, the court dismissed the city's complaint and vacated the temporary injunction, holding that the contractor was not subject to the regulations of the city's Code. The court found that the legislature had preempted the area of plans and specifications and had vested that area exclusively in the state. Having conceded that it had no control over the plans and specifications, the city was not entitled to enforce the Code against the contractor when the issuance of the required permit and the inspection as provided in the Code was meaningless. The danger of harm from the construction of schools free from local ordinances was slight as compared to the frustration of the educational mandate through delays and interference.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the city's complaint and vacated the temporary injunction prohibiting the contractor from performing plumbing work in the construction of schools until it complied with the city's ordinances.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- plumbing code -- plumbing contractor for construction of plumbing in school buildings, plans for which were prepared by licensed architect and approved as to plumbing by State Education Commissioner, is not subject to town's Plumbing Code and Ordinance requiring approval of plans and licensing of master plumber; school district also not subject to plumbing code.

The plumbing contractor employed to install the plumbing in two schools following public bidding, is not subject to a town's Plumbing Code and Ordinance which requires it to submit the plans for approval by the town, and to apply to the town for licensing, and to have a licensed master plumber on the job, where the plans for the construction of the schools were prepared by licensed architects, were approved by the school boards and by a division of the State Education Department after determining that the plumbing system conformed to standards set by the Commissioner of Education, and where the work was inspected by a trained employee of the school boards, by an employee of the architect, by the architect, and by [***2] a firm of plumbing engineers hired by the architect to inspect and test the installation. A school district is a governmental agency to which the State's responsibility for the construction of schools has been surrendered and it is not subject to a municipal building or plumbing code. The Legislature has pre-empted the area of plans and specifications for schools and vested it exclusively in the Commissioner of Education, along with the supervision of construction. The complaint in an action to enjoin the plumbing contractor and the school districts until they comply with the plumbing code is dismissed.

Asche-Bandor Corp. v. Hostetter


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


47 Misc. 2d 580; 262 N.Y.S.2d 822; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1748



June 23, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the foregoing reasons, plaintiffs' request for an injunction is denied, the complaint is dismissed and the statute complained of is declared to be constitutional.

Submit decree on notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor licensees challenged the constitutionality of N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 107-a(4), as amended by 1936 N.Y. Laws 204, § 38, which imposed license fees on licensees based on the number and category of labels of liquor they carried, in an action against defendant state liquor authority commissioners. The licensees sought an injunction banning enforcement of the law.


OVERVIEW: The licensees complained that N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 107-a(4), as amended by 1936 N.Y. Laws 204, § 38, discriminated against them as liquor wholesalers and retailers that carried many private label liquors in favor of those who handled only a few national or regional brands. The court rejected their complaint, finding that they were not damaged by the law because their business increased, rather than decreased. The court held that the registration fees set forth in the statute were not disproportionate for true license fees. The law did not result in a confiscation of the licensees' business in any sense, and the proof showed that their financial condition improved in spite of the provision. The court held that the law was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied the licensees' request for an injunction, dismissed the complaint, and declared the statute constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating liquors -- brand registration -- Alcoholic Beverage Control Law ( § 107-a, subd. 4) requiring registration of brand name and payment of fee is constitutional -- registration fees are license fees and not taxes -- plaintiffs' businesses were not confiscated by statute -- statute not discriminatory.

1. Subdivision 4 of section 107-a of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law which requires registration of brand names of alcoholic beverages and an annual registration fee of $ 100 for every liquor label, $ 50 for every beer label and $ 20 for every wine label is valid and constitutional.

2. The registration fees are license fees and are not taxes disguised as license fees.

3. Plaintiffs' businesses were not more adversely affected by the fees than their competitors. The statute does not result in confiscation of their businesses in any sense and the proof shows that their financial condition improved in spite of the statute.

4. While the statute imposes an additional cost [***2] upon plaintiffs to conduct their businesses, there is no evidence of discrimination.

 

2195 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Atlantic Beach v. Hempstead


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


47 Misc. 2d 29; 262 N.Y.S.2d 28; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1756



June 21, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an incorporated village, and defendant town filed cross-motions for summary judgment in the village's action seeking an adjudication of its authority to exercise zoning powers within the corporate limits of the village and an injunction against the exercise of such powers by the village. The village also sought such an adjudication and an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The area within the corporate limits of the village was a portion of the unincorporated area of the town prior to and on January 1, 1938, and also until the village was incorporated on June 21, 1962, pursuant to N.Y. Village Law art. 2. The town claimed exclusive zoning jurisdiction within the village pursuant to Nassau County, N.Y., County Charter § 1606 and 1607. The village filed a complaint challenging the town's right to exercise zoning powers in the village under Nassau County, N.Y., County Charter § 1606 and 1607. The town filed a counterclaim for adjudication of its rights. The court held that a reading of Nassau County, N.Y., County Charter § 2601 and the stipulated facts in the case established that no county but Nassau County could qualify under Nassau County, N.Y., County Charter § 2601 and proved that Nassau County, N.Y., County Charter §§ 1606 and 1607 were local laws, and not general statutes. There was no reasonable ground for the creation of a separate class by local law that was contrary to N.Y. Village Law art. VI-A, § 175 and N.Y. Town Law art. 16, § 261. Therefore, Nassau County, N.Y., County Charter § 1606 and 1607 violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 18.


OUTCOME: The court granted the village's motion for summary judgment, and enjoined the town from exercising zoning powers within the corporate limits of the village. The court denied the town's motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- exercise of zoning power within village -- village incorporated in 1962 has power to zone within village; sections 1606 and 1607 of County Government Law, also known as Nassau County Charter purporting to give town power to zone in territory that was part of town in 1938, including subsequently created villages, are unconstitutional and invalid as local laws.

A village incorporated in 1962 out of the unincorporated area of defendant town in Nassau County has power to zone within its own limits. Sections 1606 and 1607 of the so-called alternative form of County Government Law, also called the Nassau County Charter (L. 1936, ch. 879), which provide that the towns of Nassau County shall exercise exclusive zoning jurisdiction within all portions of the town unincorporated as villages on January 1, 1938, irrespective of their subsequent incorporation, constitute local legislation "Incorporating villages" prohibited by section 17 of article III of the New York Constitution and are invalid because of section 2601 of the said County Government Law making it applicable only to Nassau County. There was no reasonable ground in 1936 for the creation of a separate [***2] class and the enactment of a separate statute which permitted only towns in Nassau County to regulate zoning within incorporated villages contrary to article VI-A of the Village Law and article 16 of the Town Law which limit town zoning jurisdiction to areas outside the limits of any incorporated village. The words "Incorporating villages" as used in section 17 of article III of the Constitution include not only the original incorporation but the subsequent existence of a village and any legislation which affects or abridges the powers of villages pursuant to the Village Law must apply to all villages, and may not be by local law.

 

2196 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Murphy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


46 Misc. 2d 728; 260 N.Y.S.2d 739; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1780



June 14, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public employees challenged their summary dismissal from the police department for violation of New York City, N.Y., City Charter § 1123 after they refused to sign a waiver of immunity from prosecution in connection with a grand jury hearing.


OVERVIEW: Upon his appearance before the grand jury, each public employee refused to sign a waiver of immunity from prosecution and was dismissed from the police department. The public employees filed an action against respondent police commissioner and others, seeking an order of reinstatement and interim compensation. The court held that the summary dismissal of the public employees violated due process and granted the requested relief. None of the public employees was afforded an opportunity to explain, clarify, or attempt to justify his conduct or answers before the grand jury. Before they were discharged for alleged misconduct or incompetency, the public employees were each entitled to a hearing with notice of the charges against them, the right to representation by counsel, and a judicial review in accordance with N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78. It was not unconstitutional for the public employees to be dismissed for failing to waive immunity from prosecution when called upon to testify before the grand jury. The duty imposed by New York City, N.Y., City Charter § 1123 and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 6 was not an unreasonable condition of employment as a public employee.


OUTCOME: The court held that the summary dismissal of the public employees violated due process of law and ordered that the public employees be reinstated with appropriate compensation for the interim period.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- public employment -- summary discharge -- discharge of civil servants, having tenure and dismissable only after hearing on charges, summarily because of invocation of Fifth Amendment is arbitrary -- if refusal to waive Fifth Amendment rights is interpreted as prima facie basis for discharge but affording opportunity to explain, then section 1123 of New York City Charter and section 6 of article I of New York Constitution are constitutional -- offer of conditional reinstatement made to petitioners is not cure for deprivation of petitioners' due process rights -- each petitioner is entitled to reinstatement and back pay.

1. Discharge of members of the Police Department of the City of New York, civil servants entitled to tenure and dismissable only for incompetency or misconduct shown after a hearing upon due notice and stated charges, predicated solely and automatically upon the invocation of the Fifth Amendment privilege against self incrimination is arbitrary and discriminatory if the statute (New York City Charter, § 1123) falls alike on all who exercise their constitutional privilege whether the refusal to waive immunity results from mistake, inadvertence,  [***2] legal advice conscientiously given, illness or from the failure to afford the individual a reasonable opportunity to choose to speak or act in the unfettered exercise of his own will to intentionally and intelligently waive his Fifth Amendment rights.

2. If the present refusal to waive one's Fifth Amendment rights is interpreted as a prima facie rather than a conclusive basis for discharge, and as affording petitioners the opportunity to explain, then section 1123 of the New York City Charter and its counterpart in the New York Constitution (art. I, § 6) are not unconstitutional.

3. An offer for conditional reinstatement made by the Corporation Counsel is not a substitute or cure for the deprivation of petitioners' due process rights.

4. Each petitioner is entitled to reinstatement and payment of compensation for the period of his unlawful discharge.

 

2197 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Buffalo v. State Bd. of Equalization & Assessment


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


46 Misc. 2d 675; 260 N.Y.S.2d 710; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1791



June 11, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] It therefore necessarily follows that the motion of the defendants, in which defendants-intervenors have joined, is in all respects denied except that portion as it applies to the plaintiff Chester Kowal individually, and on behalf of other taxpayers similarly situated, in which respect it is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a city, its mayor, and the mayor individually and on behalf of all city taxpayers, sought a declaratory judgment that 1959 N.Y. Laws 636 and 1963 N.Y. Laws 86 were unconstitutional. Defendant New York State Board of Equalization and Assessment and defendant-intervenor railroad moved to dismiss the complaint for failure to state a cause of action and because plaintiffs did not have standing to sue.


OVERVIEW: In the action concerning real property taxation laws, the court found that the city and the mayor had standing to bring the challenge to the statutes. The imposition and collection of real property taxes was of a local nature, as well as was the establishment and disbursement of the municipal budget. The court held that in its proprietary capacity, the city should not only be subject to the restraints and standards of a private individual but conversely should be granted the rights and privileges of the latter. Such privileges included the right to question a state statute that unquestionably affected the financial structure of the city. Accordingly, the duties of the mayor were altered by the legislation under attack, and as chief executive and fiscal officer of the city, his rights were directly affected. However, mere individuals did not have standing to sue. The complaint stated a cause of action, so it was not dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion except to dismiss the mayor individually and on behalf of other taxpayers because of lack of standing.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- right to challenge constitutionality -- Mayor of city, as distinguished from Mayor as individual, and city are aggrieved persons with standing to challenge constitutionality of State statutes -- on motion to dismiss complaint before answer, declaration of rights of parties cannot be made.

1. The Mayor of a city, as distinguished from the Mayor as an individual, and the city are persons aggrieved who have standing to bring an action for judgment declaring that chapter 636 of the Laws of 1959 and chapter 86 of the Laws of 1963 are unconstitutional.

2. Since defendants have moved to dismiss the complaint for insufficiency before answer, no declaration of the rights of the parties can be made.

 

2198 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Pecora v. Queens County Bar Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


46 Misc. 2d 530; 260 N.Y.S.2d 116; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1807



June 8, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the Bar Association's motion for summary judgment is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Queens County Bar Association (Bar Association) sought summary judgment on plaintiff's suit to permanently enjoin the Bar Association from following it's plan to have a Bar Association poll to evaluate qualification and merit of candidates for judgeships and whether incumbent judges merited reelection, and if the incumbent merited reelection, to actively campaign for the judge.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed suit to enjoin the Bar Association from proceeding with its plan to conduct and publish a bar poll concerning whether incumbent judges merited reelection, to evaluate judicial candidates, and to actively campaign for incumbent judges who were voted meritorious of reelection. The court granted the Bar Association's motion for summary judgment finding that the plan was consistent with the purposes of the Bar Association, including to promote a high standard of integrity, honor, and courtesy, and it did not violate the Penal Laws.


OUTCOME: The court granted the summary judgment requested by the Bar Association in plaintiff's suit to permanently enjoin the Bar Association from evaluating judicial candidates.


HEADNOTES

Judges -- indorsement by Bar Association -- adoption by Bar Association of Queens Plan for selection of Judges is not ultra vires -- Bar Association did not violate Penal Law ( § 671) by implementing indorsement of candidate for judicial office by expending money to promote indorsed candidate.

1. Defendant Bar Association's adoption of the "Queens Plan" for the selection of Judges whereby if the members indorse a candidate for judicial office, money is expended by the Bar Association to promote his candidacy is not ultra vires. The Membership Corporations Law provides that among the purposes of a Bar Association is "facilitating the administration of justice". The Canons of Professional Ethics impose on the Bar the duty "to prevent political considerations from outweighing judicial fitness in the selection of Judges". Defendant's certificate of incorporation states that one of its purposes is to promote the due administration of justice. Its by-laws charge it to secure the election or appointment of qualified Judges.

2. Subdivision 1 of section 671 of the Penal Law forbids a corporation [***2] from using money in aid of a political party or any candidate for political office. Fairly construed, there was no legislative intent to prevent defendant Bar Association from adopting the "Queens Plan". The intent of the Legislature was to eliminate political influence secured through financial contributions by large corporations. The Bar Association did not violate section 671. It is inconceivable that the Legislature would prescribe that one of the corporate purposes of a Bar Association is to facilitate the administration of justice and then make criminal the activity designed to effectuate that purpose. Moreover, there was no political purpose involved in defendant's indorsement of a candidate, for it did not refer to the candidate's political affiliation but only the candidate himself.

 

2199 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re City of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


46 Misc. 2d 558; 260 N.Y.S.2d 229; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1897



May 18, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mortgagor filed an action with the court to compel respondent mortgagee to accept payment of the unpaid principal amount of its mortgage out of an advance payment of an award for a property being taken by the city.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor sought to compel the mortgagee to accept payment of the unpaid principal of its mortgage out of an advance payment pursuant to the property's taking by the city with a four percent interest rate, in contravention to the six percent rate agreed upon by the parties in their contract. The court ruled in favor of the mortgagee. The court held that New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B15-37.0 regarding the termination of contractual obligations pursuant to a taking by the city concerned only those covenants that touched and concerned the interest of the parties in the real property, not the award. The court stated that the compensation did not touch or concern the real estate. The freedom to contract was abridged only where the enforcement of the contract conflicted with dominant public interests. The court noted that the contract at bar involved no such interest or situation invoking the police power to promote or preserve the health, safety, and welfare of the public. The court held that the parties were free to contract for an apportionment of the award that reduced the share of that award going to the mortgagor in favor of the mortgagee.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the mortgagee in the mortgagor's action to compel payment of the principal and interest of the mortgage.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Eminent domain -- apportionment of award -- mortgagor of condemned property contracted with mortgagee, prior to condemnation, that, in event thereof, mortgagor would pay principal plus 6% interest per annum to date of maturity; section B15-37.0 of Administrative Code of City of New York discharging contracts affecting condemned real property does not discharge such provision since it does not affect realty but only award -- by filing claim in condemnation, mortgagee does not seek greater award from city but seeks enforcement of mortgagor's contract -- no unjust enrichment of mortgagee is involved.

1. The owner of property, prior to its condemnation, entered into a mortgage loan agreement with the mortgagee which provided that, in the event of condemnation, the owner would pay the mortgagee the difference in interest received from the City of New York and the 6% per annum provided by the mortgage from the date of condemnation to the date of the maturity of the loan, May 7, 1967. Such clause in the mortgage does not fall because of section B15-37.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York, which provides that, where a parcel of real property is taken in condemnation,  [***2] all contracts touching the same shall be discharged upon the vesting of title in the city. The covenants discharged are those touching the interests of the parties in the real property and not in the award. The clause in the mortgage here deals with apportionment of the award and does not concern the real estate or add to the obligation of the sovereign with respect to the award. There is no public policy preventing mortgagor and mortgagee from providing, although the city is required to pay interest at 4%, that out of the award the mortgagee can take its unpaid principal and 6%, thereby reducing the share of the award going to the mortgagor. To interpret section B15-37.0 as nullifying the clause would result in an invalid application of an existing statute to the rights of parties to freely contract under Federal and State Constitutions due process clauses. ( Fliegel v. Manhattan Sav. Bank, 296 N. Y. 214, distinguished.)

2. Even though the mortgagee has filed a claim in the condemnation proceeding, thereby electing to look to the city for payment, the mortgagee does not seek an additional award to be paid by city funds but seeks payment of the mortgage plus 6% to maturity [***3] out of the advance payment made to the mortgagor.

3. Freedom to contract in a market where lenders are in the keenest competition to place funds and the parties bargain in equality should not be invaded nor frustrated by mortgagor's plea of unjust enrichment which is in direct conflict with what the parties voluntarily contemplated.

 

2200 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cambist Films, Inc. v. Board of Regents


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


46 Misc. 2d 513; 260 N.Y.S.2d 804; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1920



May 12, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner distributor sought a judgment, directing respondent Board of Regents of the University of the State of New York to issue a license for its film. The Board counterclaimed, seeking a declaration that: (1) the film was obscene within the meaning of N.Y. Educ. Law § 122; and (2) N.Y. Educ. Law §§ 120-132 and the Board's Rule 221, N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 8, § 12.9, as adopted March 26, 1965 were valid and constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The distributor applied to the Board for a license to exhibit its film. The Board's motion picture division found certain scenes to be obscene. The distributor requested a re-examination. The director of the division sustained the original determination. The distributor appealed to the Board and a committee thereof sustained the director's decision. The court noted that the U.S. Supreme Court had held that a system of movie censorship was required to contain certain procedural safeguards if it was not to run afoul of the First Amendment. These safeguards included a requirement that the censor have the burden of instituting judicial proceedings. The court held the statutory procedure for review in New York, incorporated in N.Y. Educ. Law § 124, was unconstitutional because it provided that a determination to deny a license was reviewable by a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding instituted by the applicant. The Board's rules also failed to contain the required procedural safeguards. However, in the absence of legislative authority incorporating the required procedural safeguards in the New York statutory scheme, the court declined to direct the issuance of a license to the distributor.


OUTCOME: The court denied the relief requested by the distributor, dismissed the portion of the Board's counterclaim that requested the court to declare the film obscene within the meaning of the Education Law, and declared that the procedure for review of films contained in the Education Law and the Board's Rules was invalid and unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- motion picture licensing statutes -- Education Law ( §§ 120-132) and section 221 of Rules of Board of Regents providing for censorship and licensing of motion pictures are unconstitutional -- argument that license must be issued for petitioner's motion picture rejected -- proceeding not transferred for determination to Appellate Division.

1. The film-licensing statute contained in part II of article 3 ( §§ 120-132) of the Education Law, and section 221 of the Rules of the Board of Regents adopted thereunder, are unconstitutional in view of the decision in Freedman v. Maryland (380 U.S. 259), in that the statute lacks (1) authority for the Board of Regents to institute "within a specified brief period" judicial action "to restrain showing the film" in the event that a license is not issued administratively since the "burden of proving that the film is unprotected expression must rest on the censor" and not upon the applicant as section 124 of the Education Law now establishes; and (2) a judicial procedure to "assure a prompt final judicial decision, to minimize the deterrent effect of an interim and possibly erroneous denial of a license", a safeguard [***2] of definite time limits to be imposed by the Legislature. By its rule 221, the Board of Regents sought to change the effect of section 124 of the Education Law which provides that the applicant for the license must commence the judicial review proceeding, which change the board may not effect by rules.

2. Petitioner's argument that a license must be directed for its film upon the ground that licensing per se is not unconstitutional is rejected. Such a direction would force the court to impel approval of a motion picture found to be obscene by the Board of Regents.

3. The nature of this proceeding and current case law requires that the proceeding be passed upon by the court and not remitted to the Appellate Division for determination.
